Looking at Cindy's Long trade:

Perfect M5 group entry at 15:20 (15:15 chart time +7 EST)

We have Risk 0% (5 green lights) so we must switch to M15 group

We must close the M15 candle so we need to assess at close at 15:30 (15:15 M15 chart time). Here we have Risk 20% because our Origin Line remains below 23.6%..so we must close another M15 candle.

The first chart is the M15 candle at close at 15:45 (15:30 M15 chart time). Notice that we have all green lights Risk 0%, so we must now flip to the M30 group.

The second chart is our M30 candle close at 16:00 because we flipped over at 15:45 we musrt wait for the M30 to close to assess. Look at M30 and we get a completely different story where we have Risk 60% so we must exit.

This brings us out at +18 PIPS.

Let me explain what is happening here. Our M30 is in an oversold market, and we want to make sure that when we stay in a long we are breaking out of this oversold market. The M30 Market has not kept pace with our M5 and M15 market...and thus M5 and M15 will rebound down and either we'll move on and stay oversold or M5 and M15 will try and break up again. As such with our M30 position lagging our risk jumps up significantly in this long trade. We expect it to rise above 23.6 and start an escalator up move, but in this case either we will be far too early or it isn't going to happen.

Knowing what we know, a 60% risk assesment is just about bang on....6/10 times this M30 long trade will fail where it is and 4/10 times it will succeed. I think if you look at it as failing completely or being too early to enter the long you'd find this risk assessment fairly close (maybe +/- 5%) statistically to what really happens historically.

If you were watching the M5,M15 and M30 groups at the same time, you can easily detect the elasticity in the M5 group on this trade. If we are more advanced we go short on the M5 elasticity and try and run through an oversold trade...this is far off our mechanical system...but an option with the Brain Indicator.

2 red boxes do not count as 2 bad indications...they count only as one.  In our short trade......our Price Line is either above 76.4% or it is not.

--- 帖子 #978 ---
Very nice analysis work.  Since we are building a mechanical system let me put this in a more mechanical terminology....our system is much more like a transmission that fits to the market engine.

You are correct that the M5 Group is strictly an entry group.  When our conditions are met we switch gears...we move up to the next time frame.  If we jump into car talk, we've hit maximum revolutions and we are red lining...time to shift.

The M15 and M30 group is our driving gears...we will stay in these groups much longer and they will consistently provide us with enough torque and power range to trade throught the hills and valleys we must drive through.  Sometimes our engine runs out of gas or overheats and dies...so do our trades.   But on a day-to-day basis we know that we'll just chug along and keep moving.

Our levels are not arbitrary....well,... within reason.  You could easily say that we must cross 83 or 72  or even 90 and 10.  There is not only balance in chosing the levels but there is the overall market...the big dollars that ply their trade on the tradional 80/20 numbers.  These numbers are measures of the overmarket.

I select 76.4 and 23.6 because they are Fib numbers.  They are also a little further away from the traditional overmarket levels.  Do Fib numbers have meaning?  I think so.  There is simply to much coincidence to ignore with Fibs.

The shift from time frame to time frame using the  same levels is because we must apply the same rules to ourr overmarket conditions.  The over market rules do not change with time frames....however, our Price and Over market conditions do change through the time frames.  This is because each time frame stochastically has a different range between high and low.

Our mecahnical system is looking for "convergence" of the price and stochastics.  This is what I showed you in the rope theory.  When we have convergence we move out of the overmarket.

The mechanical system is using this same rope theory but instead of trying to figure out 26 stochastic lines on one chart I have simply broken it up over 4 groups of time frames.

Obviously, I have had to put some compromises in to make this work and to make the system mechanical enough.  I would not trade such a mechanical system...not becuse it won't work but simply becuase I can read the other time frames and put a complete picture together in my head much easier.

Having said that, the levels are consistent with the rules of overmarket conditions for each time frame.

The "pure luck" is not luck at all, but convergence of our stochastics when our stochastics are in the same relative position through the time frames.

The filter is a tool to help us at least confirm we have one lower time frame in an opposite overmarket condition before we enter a trade..or change time frames.  It is a filter and is used to keep our win percentage high in a mechanical trade.

The crossover is a very powerful indicator between time frames and reading all about the M5 trigger will tell you what is happening and how short time frames build longer time frames.

The 80/20 cross is the historical basis of overmarket exit conditions and also the fundamnetal rule in Escalator to Pips that is a tried and true condition over multiple time frames that support long trends.

The Price Line is our momentum indicator and being at the extremes tells us it is exhausted and will move..as will oscillate the slowest between 0 and 100 we know that using shorter time frames to trade around it will keep us within its boundaries.  We want it at the extremes becuase it is predictable...at 50% it can go anywhere.

I think if you look at the grapghs (charts) you included you will see there is consistency there, just it is different than the way you are looking at it.  (look at the overall picture).

The mechanical system doesn't work by coincidence or luck.  I have explained every theory and transition in many thread postings before.  I'll accept that not everyone is going to understand or use everything I write.  I present it in different ways so that if someone doesn't understand the rope, they might understand this mechanical system better.

This mechanical system is the same rope, escalator, M5 trigger idealologies presented in a very "put your entry here", "take an exit here" way.  In the mechanical system you see 5 combinations are true and switch time frames and if we have less than 3 combinations true in a time frame we exit.

The combinations are not knew they are just the overmarket rules.

The fact that they line up for long trends is just the convergence of the rope.

The consistent crossover after crossover, across 80, across 80 of each time frame is just escalator to pips

The 5 conditions to enter on M5 is just the M5 trigger (slightly modified).

The 2/5 conditions to exit (rather than 3/5 to stay in) is because our rope has spread and our price move is breaking down

The picking of the Origin Line opposite to the Price Line is elasticity

The Picking of Price Line and Origin line together at the oversold/overmarket extreme is escalator to pips, rope theory convergence, and overmarket reversal

The mechanical system is taking a lot out of each system.  Not the math, but the decision making process of identifying the stochastic moves and how they relate to each other.  That does not make the mechanical system one of luck or one that will never lose....it is simply a tool to learn how to trade stochastics with and if one uses it that way...they will succeed.

Any inconsistencies that do exist are out in to keep the trade in a safe magin...the goal of the mechanical system is to make pips consistently, lose as little pips as possible and keep drawdown to a minimum.  All of that is going to come with trade offs such as getting out of trades earlier than we want, entering trades later than we want, and in some cases accepting minimum PIP gains when more are available.

The mechanical system will never be perfect.  It can be tweaked, supecharged, add a some slicks, to do different things..to be more aggressive or likewise we can tinker it down and make it safer.  But it does have to follow fundamental rules to work.

--- 帖子 #985 ---
Well, you have answered your own question in your question.  "...but the 30m is in no way set up for an escalator and in turn will obviously not meet an acceptable risk% at its next close".

The question back to you is why stay in this trade?  Trading is a game of risk management...the advantage of trading over gambling is that we can stack the house in our favour...at casinos we can't.

If you are up pips why risk them knowing that this trade is going nowhere...oh you might miss some more pips or it might just do something crazy and turn the M30 around....but what are the odds of that happening?

If your down a little you might try for a breakeven or losing your spread exit...or at least try and exit minimizing your losses.

But overall, over the long haul we are better just to exit.  Sometimes we'lll kick ourselves for exiting but in the long run statistically we'll be further ahead.

My moto is never risk pips made if you are in "hope mode" for more pips and the charts are telling you to get out.

If you want to be stubborn and trade M15..then I'd trade the price level by fibs..so in a short as long as the orgin or price line is falling through the fibs and does not retrace 1 fib level up you stay in..but if it does retrace up 1 fib level you are out...if the origin line is oversold and the price level is falling, then if the origin comes up past 23.6 your done (you can set any level you like..say 20 or even 15...if you hit positive targets then tighten up the negative ones...say it retraces 1/2 fib up you exit after it drops a full fib....kinda thing.  Look for small targets to be reached and set strong indicators in you rmind for an exit in this case....so you don't go into him/haw mode...say if it reaches 20...if that's your exit then exit...in this kinda case.

If you simply get an M5 entry then just enter if you want to do it mechanically...just keep entering M5 on entry signals and thnen progress and exit each trade as normal...this may mean exiting some on M15 while staying in M30.  We have to keep in mind that whipsaws may throw us out of an M15 much quicker than an M30 where we might ride the whipsaw through and get a prolonged longer trend even when M5 and M15 no longer support any more of the trade...likely they are stuck in an overmarket

--- 帖子 #1011 ---
Hi Sarah certainlly...

lets take the first example where we had the 1m/5m/15m signal... The risk here is calculated as 0% so immediatly change our 1m/5m/15m set up to a 5m/15m/30m set up, wait for the next 15m close and then assess the risk at that time...

How did we get a 0% calculation on the first entry?....

Think of it in 5 parts and each part is worth 20% (5x20% = 100%)

The 5 parts of our long trade:

1 - The Price line - Is it above 76.4% or below 23.6% ? In this case the Price line is below 23.6% - Our risk is still 0%

2 - The Origion line - Has it crossed above 23.6%? It has so our risk remains 0%

3 -The 15m 14,3,3 - Has it gone above 20? It has so our risk remains at 0%

4 - Has the 5m crossed the 15m in our direction? It has so our risk remains 0%

5 - Is our 1m filter where we want it to (above 80) ? It is so our risk remains at 0%

That means our total risk = 0% and we can now enter the trade and switch to the 15m - wait for the close and do the same risk assesment on the 15m

So I guess to summarise - If one of the 5 conditions above are not met then we add 20% to our risk

For example...

If 3 conditions are not met it would make our risk 60% (3x20%)

If 2 are not met our risk becomes 40% (2x20%)

Hope this helps it's a lot easier than I might have made it sound here

--- 帖子 #1012 ---
So now the 1 hour candle has closed and the risk is 20% so we hold the trade.

20% risk is because the only condition of our 5 that was not met was our 30m Filter has not crossed 80%

everything else was met...

30m filter has not crossed 80% + 20%

the H1 has crossed the H4, + 0%

The Price line is below 23.6, + 0%

The 30m 14,3,3 has crossed 20, +0%

and the origion line has crossed 23.6 +0%

--- 帖子 #1041 ---
We use 14,1,1 on M5 can we use it on higher time frames?

First, there is no reason why you can't use 14,1,1 on the higher time frames, but let me explain why I don't.

14,1,1 is a fast stochastic and as such much more jittery.  The benefits of 14,1,1 in the M5 entry group is that we are using it for entry.  In otherwords, we are not following it after we enter.  These faster (sharper) moves give us a little quicker response to our entry.

When we pop up to M15 and M30 we want to stay in the trade and avoid whipsaws.  On M15 we keep M5 a little faster on the filter just to help it keep pace a bit.  However, the M15 is our trending chart and we want to avoid being affected by whipsaws.  In otherwords, the smoother 14,3,3 line will hold us in just a little longer for M30 and H1.

If I were going to adjust, I'd go all 14,3,3....this would be a slightly more conservative approach.  I think you'd find far less benefits in the higher time frames of using 14,1,1 during the trade.  It is my observation but feel free to experiment.

--- 帖子 #1043 ---
Very nice analysis Cindy...you played that trade about the exact same as me.

I think this is fairly obvious but I might mention it, if we move up a time frame and our risk is too high but we can stay in the lower time frame than you can do that.  If you roll back all the way to M5 and it is at Risk 0 in the same trade direction...we obviously stay in the trade and go to M15 since this is an entry.

This can happen if say M30 is lagging a bit but looks like it will go our way and M15 is still ok risk wise.  It can get a little riskier this way....I prefer them rolling over into each other but with 4 chart groups up it should be fairly easy to see where we are and if the risk is worth taking.

Entries and staying in trades can be at any time the Risk is 0, 20 or 40.  Exits can be at Risk 20, 40, 60, 80 ,100...it is simply how much risk you want in your trade.   For the mechanical system I drew the line on one set of rules to make it simple.  However, in mutliple charts and using our brains you can constantly assess the risk level of each time frame for our trade.

What you are looking for is "rollover" to each higher time frame...if you can rollover to each higher time frame and maintain Risk 0, 20, 40 on each rollover say M15, to M30 for example but M15 has not gone Risk 0 yet and then H1 goes say Risk 20...then you can stay on M15 or bump yourself up to M30.  Don't be afraid to travek through the time frames..it just gives you finer focus on your trade...the higher time frames smooth out the whipsaws and the lower time frames allow you to time your exit.

--- 帖子 #1056 ---
Hello sarah,

One way would be to close a percentage of your trade, say 50%, at a likely first profit target, say +10 pips.  Then set your stop loss to b/e or b/e +1.

If price comes back to hit your s/l you have already banked a profit and simply wait for the next entry.

If price continued in your direction then close 50% of the remaining trade at a second likely target, say +20 pips.  You may then either leave your s/l where it is or move it to +10 pips.

The remaining portion of your trade may then remain open until you receive a signal to close it from whichever chart you are now on.

This method will sometimes allow a portion of your trade to remain open WHEN and not if stop hunting is going on, after which you can re-enter the market and add to your position should you get a new M5 entry signal in the original direction of the trade, something which Spud has eluded to in the past but not yet covered in detail.

The +10 and +20 figures that I used are for example only as we all trade slightly differently, some waiting an extra 20 seconds for confirmation and possibly losing a few pips while others will be in 20 seconds before candle close using the Brain Indicator to anticipating the move and making a few extra pips.  Ideally we should all be keeping our own stats to tell us what these figures, together with our initial entry s/l, should be for our own trading style.

Food for thought: 10 pips a day on 1 full lot = £/$/€100 a day

10 pips a day on 10 full lots = £/$/€1,000 a day

10 pips a day on 100 full lots = £/$/€10,000 a day

Should we be sitting in front of a computer 24/5 trying to make a gazillion pips each day or refining our technique to allow us to make 10 pips in the first hour of trading allowing us to enjoy the remainder of the time as we think best .  I suspect that Spud is trying to teach us the latter

--- 帖子 #1065 ---
If you haven't noticed, this system is designed to trade off the peaks. One way to time your entries and look at the entire picture is to look to see if we are trading off a peak or not.

The advantage of trading off the peak is that it does allow you to keep a fairly tight stop loss and minimize.

If you look back at my balls you'll recognize this pattern over the time frames. The prelude to an off the peak short entry is that everything is in the M5 Group is maxing out at the top. Likewise with the M15 group and the M30 group..the 2 exceptions are the H1 and H4. Rememeber that our shorter time frames must fall first down to H1 and H4 before H1 and H4 can continue to climb.

The second chart shows our M5 Group entry..you can see how we come off the peak and how our M5 Group setsup to clear us out of the overbought market. When the downward move starts to near it's end you will see M5 and M15 start to put up the roadblocks (not shown).

You can attack these off the peak moves by putting your S/L at the high of the peak and setting your profit within the market range...i.e. if it is a tight range...keep the profits small. Put a second trade in to catch to play the trend and wait for the Risk to get to high.

Hello Everyone!

I'm new to this Thread,

is little more than a week that I don't post on the forum, because I was trying to understand and to test the Spud method.

I must say that seems very interesting and I decided to try to make an indicator that follows the directions given by Spud.

My approach to coding is fairly recent, I have modified other indicators, I hope this goes well enough.

After three days of coding that is the result.

Well, the indicator shows the combinations of time frames, i have added also TF1.

The combinations are:
For up trend

Price line < 23.6 and Origin line > 23.6 green signal

price line > 76.4 Origin line and  < 23.6 green signal

Stoch crossing: Stoch1> Stoch2 and Stoch1 > 20 green signal

Filter line > 76.4
For Down Trend:

Price line> 76.4 Origin line and  < 76.4 signal red

price line < 23.6 and Origin line > 76.4 signal red

Stoch crossing: Stoch1 < Stoch2 and Stoch1 < 80 red signal

Line Filter < 23.6.

If there aren't these combinations the signal is neutral.

Try the indicator and tell me if it works well or if there are changes to be done, I have not had much time to try it, I just finished it.

Good Luck.

Lubo

--- 帖子 #1076 ---
Ok, let's take a look at the overall picture of where we are and what we are trading. Between triggers, ropes and escalators it can be confusing.

The simple definition is we are trading the breakout from the over market. We are doing this to catch a new trend.

Complicate this and we are trading the oscillations within a trend that builds a trend or reverses a trend. In otherwords we are trading just about everything possible to trade. We even ride the overmarket when we are in a trade if we desire.

But let's keep this simple, as this is what we built the mechanical system to be.

Our best strategy is to trade off the peak of the price move. If you follow the mechanical system you can see this is what we are doing "most" of the time and we can certainly restrict our trades to seek peaks. Again, we can get very complicated chasing daily peaks, trading with trends, etc. but let's just play the off the peak trade.

The first chart identifies a standard M5 long entry with a Risk 0. If you back up a 2 candles from our long entry you can see the price peak and the stochastic peak. (If you recall the rope this is our peak).

The lowest point on this peak is our resistance line. As such I would set a stop at least 10 pips below our resistance line. This is NOT a pre-programed stop...this is a stop in your brain. There is no reason to tell our broker our true stop and get spiked out. Our set stop is set at between 50-100 pips this is our physical stop to protect our account from an emergency. The odds of actually hitting this stop are in the 99 percentile or better if you enter on an R0 with M5.

We use the 10 pip below our peak stop as something we use to exit if we cannot see any hope of our trade going our way...where our risk is too high (R60-R100).

In the trade we are using our time frames to assess our risk. We start with the M5 group to enter. We want the M15 group to take-over. In a perfect world this will happen quickly in M15 (1-2 M15 candles from entry). There is nothing wrong with riding M5 and observing risk, but we should always finish an M15 candle that looks like it "might" support our trade and have risk R0 to R40 risk. Obviously the same holds true for M30 and H1 groups. As long as we can justify our risk on a time frame we can stay in the trade. The higher the time frame we move up...the more we are trend trading.

There is no such thing as an early exit. If a trend is goint to continue you will get multiple entry signals and just keep trading them.

Your single objective in trading this sytem is to enter of the peak in the right direction. Imagine if you can do that 99/100 times and gain 5 pips a trade.

IT IS NOT HOW MANY PIPS YOU MAKE...IT IS ABOUT HOW MUCH YOUR PIPS ARE WORTH. Let me put it this way...if you enter a trade and you know you can't lose...how much money would you trade? As much as you can find! If you are entering a trade and have no confidence where it will go, how much will you trade? $1 a pip and as tight a stop as possible. What will win more and what will win you more?

You can easily make 20 pips a day on this system and if you follow it and are picky about your entry you will learn to do it with 100% confidence. Not only do we have signals, we have patterns and these patterns show up over and over on every good trade. You have to practice.

Anyways, ignore me if you wish and feed your ego on 200 pip trades...but ego doesn't make money in trading.

So back to the chart below. When we enter; the M5 group stays betwen R0 to R40 until the close of the second M15 candle where M15 takes over at R20 and M5 dies at R80. So the question is do you exit at M5 being R80 or do you stay at M15 R20? Are you positive pips? Is M5 showing signs for a short? Did we hit our mental stop? No. No. No. So go on to M15 and watch M5 for any reversal short entry. If your losing pips exit if you have an reversal signal, you hit your mental stop, or there is no hope of your trade continuing to support you.

The second chart is M15 and you can see we get in an up trend with M15. M5 and M15 settle on low risk levels for some time and this is easy to follow.

If you are going to trade to an exit indicator it is when M5 brings up a R0 for a short trade as shown on the M15. You have lots of pips so get out. Don't even bother using M30 Group. Take your pips and get out. If the long trend is going to continue you will get a new long signal...or trade the M5 short and use the M5 peak to set your stop on the short.

You can use any number of exit criteria....just remember the more pips you chase the more you risk.

Move your stop up? This is up to you and how you want to play. You can trade 2 lots...one for sniping and one for trending. This will likely keep your trend chasing loses to a minimum. I like to guarantee myself 5 pips a trade but not at the expense of getting to tight on my stop. I suggest at least a 15 pip spread..so up 20 set your mental stop at 5.

I snipe...I'd much rather trade 20 trades within a trend and make a pile of pips along the way than trade 1 trade and hope this is "the trend". I have no idea if I'll make 200 pips on this trade...but I know I when I enter I will make 5-20 pips almost all the time.

Summary:

Set your S/L 10 pips from the lowest low/highest high at the peak.

Enter with R0 on M5 and after (off) a peak

Try to upgrade to M15 but watch M5 for revesal signs

Exit on positive pips...don't get greedy take it in small trades and many steps rather than just 1 trade

Find your exit..pick pips, fib lines, revesral....just remember if you are chasing pips you raise your risk

Having problems? Post your charts, I'll help you.

--- 帖子 #1079 ---
Feeding the thoughts!

WELL THIS IS A LONG POST  --  PROPERLY FOR SOME DAYS MY FEW LAST ONCE !!

I thought I will share with my implementation of Spuds MTF Stochastic!

I want to warn you - this follows basically Spud's rules - but some twists by me: mainly because I like it or I do not see any other reason worth.

I share that for two reason:

1. Maybe there is something - which feeds your thoughts in implementing your design of it - or which will overall improve or simplify something.

2. Maybe I got somewhere mixed up - and you have reasonable thoughts of improvement.

OK MJ's present implementation.:

PMTF Stochastics With Time Frame Shift:

A implementation with an emergency StopLoss - BUT no Trailing - Exit is purely by Risk assessment (or Hit of EmergensyStopLoss)

1. Stoch Settings: I follow strictly Spud's Stoch settings

REASON:

a. I thought first the different settings applied to different TF-goups was a mistake - but Spud reasoned it was by design.

b. I think for the beginning it is best to use the same settings Spud proved in his own trading - if things will be successful as hoped for - I still can play with changing the settings.     # TimeFrameLevel1: TF-goup M5

FilterTimeFrame=M1  (Stoch_Filter (14,3,3))

MainTimeFrame=M5  (PriceLine (100,3,3), OriginLine (14,3,3), Stoch_Main (14,1,1))

HighTimeFrame=M15  (Stoch_HighFrame (14,3,3))

# TimeFrameLevel2: TF-goup M15

FilterTimeFrame=M5  (Stoch_Filter (14,1,1))

MainTimeFrame=M15  (PriceLine (100,3,3), OriginLine (14,3,3), Stoch_Main (14,3,3))

HighTimeFrame=M30  (Stoch_HighFrame (14,3,3))

# TimeFrameLevel3: TF-goup M30

FilterTimeFrame=M15  (Stoch_Filter (14,3,3))

MainTimeFrame=M30  (PriceLine (100,3,3), OriginLine (14,3,3), Stoch_Main (14,3,3))

HighTimeFrame=H1  (Stoch_HighFrame (14,3,3))

# TimeFrameLevel4: TF-goup H1

FilterTimeFrame=M30  (Stoch_Filter (14,3,3))

MainTimeFrame=H1  (PriceLine (100,3,3), OriginLine (14,3,3), Stoch_Main (14,3,3))

HighTimeFrame=H3 or H4  (Stoch_HighFrame (14,3,3))

* note my broker does not support H4 so I use H3 instead

2. Risk Assessment:  I follow strictly Spud's Risk assessment

REASON:

makes sense to me - for the higher TF-groups OriginLine and Stoch_Main are the same and one could simplify it: I do for different reason keep it separated. SHORT_RISK

SHORT_PriceLine_above_76_4_OR_below_23_6

SHORT_OriginLine_crossed_below_76_4

SHORT_Stoch_Main_below_80

SHORT_Stoch_Main_crossed_below_Stoch_HighFrame

SHORT_Stoch_Filter_below_23_6

LONG_RISK

LONG_PriceLine_above_76_4_OR_below_23_6

LONG_OriginLine_crossed_above_23_6

LONG_Stoch_Main_above_20

LONG_Stoch_Main_crossed_above_Stoch_HighFrame

LONG_Stoch_Filter_above_76_4
* ADDITION: 'Entry_MinDistance'  at the time of entering a new Trade I do a check for a min distance of Stoch_M5 :For LONG this is the difference to the 100 for Short Distance to the 0 Stochastic number.

e.g 'Entry_MinDistance' = 30 means: For a SHORT entry the Stoch_M5 MUST be additionally above 30, For LONG entry the Stoch_M5 MUST be additionally below 70

REASON: as I do run a fully automatic system - I had it sometimes that all Risk where 0 but the Stoch_M5 had reached already the other side which I did not think I want for obvious reason.

I count Risk Levels like that: e,g: before risk assessment I set

SHORT_RISK = 5  - I assume at start of assessment always Highest Risk- until I proved it to be lower.

for each failed check I subtract 1.

So my Risk Levels go from 0 - 5

Acceptable Risk Level is 0,1 and 2.

The additional  'Entry_MinDistance' is not counted in by the Risk Levels (to be consistent over TF_groups) but only applied separately for new Trades.

3. NEW TRADES ENTRY:

My broker does not allow SHORT and LONG Trades in one account: So I use 2 Accounts - one for only Short trades the other for only Long trades.

a. I only enter new trades on TF_group M5 ->  and only if on this particular TF_group and Account there is not already a open trade: (you will understand better what I mean when I come to Switching TF-groups.

b. I enter new trades only by  3 assesments:

TF-group M5 must have Risk level: 0

additional  'Entry_MinDistance' : must be met

only if there is NO open trade on TF_group M5  at the moment (for that Account)

REASON: only if there is NO open trade on TF_group M5  at the moment (for that Account)

I re asses the Risk Levels every Minute (actually 5 seconds after a full min - so to have just a closed Candle)

If TF_group M5 had just Risk 0 and I enter a New trade - it properly will have Risk 0 in the next minutes  check again - I would get too many multiply Trades for actually one clear Entry. (There are many ways to solve this - I did it as described above)

you will see that I fully allow multiply trades. Theoretically there could be hundreds of Long and hundreds of Short trades open at the same time.

If all Trades are on higher TF_groups I enter still New trades: Short and Long whatever comes

4. Time Frame Group Switch and EXIT: I differ here quite a bit from Spud.

REASON:

For me it makes more sense to switch Time Frame Levels (TF-groups) when the acceptable Risk is broken.

my Acceptable risk is: Risk 0,1, or 2  (by my Risk assesment as defined above)

EXIT: I exit never by moving Trailing StopLoss or TakeProfit Trades (StopLoss is purely emergency here)

I exit only by Risk assesment.

Basically I implemented 3 version (2 are quite similar) of Time Frame Group Switch to choose from:

I think they advance go from safest to most risky TF_group switch (remember I don't trail StopLoss)1 TimeFrameLevel_ChangeType 1 Rule: Stay on current TF-group until Risk reaches 60% or more (by my definition: 3 or more) --> re-asses immediately next higher TF-group - if Risk below 60 % move Trade up otherwise close --> when Last TF-group Risk reaches 60% or more always exit.

2 TimeFrameLevel_ChangeType 2: Rule: Stay on current TF-group until Risk reaches 60% or more --> re-asses immediately next higher TF-group - if Risk below 60 % move Trade up otherwise close --> when Last TF-group Risk reaches 60% or more  - re-asses immediately the very first TF-group - if Risk below 60 % move Trade to it otherwise close --> and we start the Circle from the beginning

REASON 2: just a small twist to number 1 --> basically I just liked the though of possible theroretically entering an ever ongoing profitable trade ;-)

3 TimeFrameLevel_ChangeType 3: Rule: Stay on current TF-group until Risk reaches 60% or more --> re-asses immediately next higher TF-group - if Risk below 60 % move Trade up otherwise -- check in an order (always to the next lower TF-group) if any of the lower TF-groups have a supportive Risk Level if so move the Trade to it (and continue as before) - if the next Higher TF-group and NO Lower TF group have a supportive Risk level close the trade (never over jump a TF-group  higher - but you can overjump lower TF-roups.

REASON 3: I think overjumping higher TF_groups add to my risk as there are substantially higher reversal within the still acceptable Risk assessment. - whereas going to Lower TF_groups does not have such a problem.

Side Note: only with  TimeFrameLevel_ChangeType 3 I can have multiple trades on TF_group M5 (in case I move Trades down).

There are other things as possible money management ect - but I think I shared most of the trading rules

I should say: That I'm still not 100% convinced if Switching Time Frames makes really sense  and is necessary to get the optimum of profit. Because of that I also implemented a second version.

PMTF Stochastics Without Time Frame Shift_USING Trailing StopLoss:
REASON:

Thought is like that: A trade itself has no idea about TF http://www.forexfactory.com/images/icons/icon12.gif

So if a trade follows certain rules (like the one presented by Spud MTF Stochastic) it will do so if we switch or if we do not switch TF.

So it would seem to me reasonable to apply the same Entry rules on TF_group M5 and than just forget all thoughts about TF and use a trailing StopLoss.

Tricky thing is to get the optional StopLoss so to not get Stopped out too early -- but also not too far away to loose halve of our profit if the Trade turns.

SO: for my second VERION: PMTF Stochastics Without Time Frame Shift_USING Trailing StopLoss

1. I use ONLY TF_group M5 and only to define New Trade entries.

2. I apply the exact same rules for Trade Entry as in the other system.

Note: (this means I can not have multiply trades in one account) max is one Long and one Short trade open at the same time.

3. I still set the exact emergency StopLoss in the beginning.

4. I have added an optional parameter to set a fixed Take Profit by Trade Entry. just to use it if wanted - if used it changes to some extend  the reason for the trailing stop loss.

5. most important in this approach: TRAILING STOP LOSS SYSTEM:

I can think of different possiblilities to do a flexible system:

The one I implemented: conficuration is like this:"TrailingStopLoss" : [

{ 'MinProfitInPips' : 12, 'TrailingStopLossPercentage' : 17},

{ 'MinProfitInPips' : 20, 'TrailingStopLossPercentage' : 30},

{ 'MinProfitInPips' : 30, 'TrailingStopLossPercentage' : 45},

{ 'MinProfitInPips' : 40, 'TrailingStopLossPercentage' : 50},

{ 'MinProfitInPips' : 60, 'TrailingStopLossPercentage' : 60},

{ 'MinProfitInPips' : 80, 'TrailingStopLossPercentage' : 60},

{ 'MinProfitInPips' : 100, 'TrailingStopLossPercentage' : 70},

{ 'MinProfitInPips' : 120, 'TrailingStopLossPercentage' : 80},

{ 'MinProfitInPips' : 150, 'TrailingStopLossPercentage' : 85},

{ 'MinProfitInPips' : 170, 'TrailingStopLossPercentage' : 90},

],

One can add as many settings or as few as one wants - completly adjustable.

REASON:

I one uses a fixed let's say 50% Trailing Stop Loss you get this problem:

a. In the beginning where one is just 10 or 20 PIPS up it is too close and get's easily hit.

b. later on if one was lucky to nmake it throught the first stage and say we are up 150 PIPs it is too far aways and if the trade turns against you would have in the end just (50% from 150 = 75) 75 PIPs.

With adjusting the Trailing StopLoss by percentage of profit this is somewhat taken care for.

There would be a even more delicate way to do it and adjust it all purelly by percentage like:

{ 'MinProfitInPips' : 12, 'MinTrailingStopLossPercentage' : 17, MaxProfitInPips: 200, MaxTrailingStopLossPercentage' : 95, }

And than calulate dynamicaly at any point the correct Percentage When we Reach our MaxProfitInPips: 200 - we reached also our MaxTrailingStopLossPercentage -- after that we just keep it by MaxTrailingStopLossPercentage.

If you get what I mean.

I implemented my version of Trailing Stop Loss because I wanted to set key points. and not only be linear.

So: I will still need a couple of days to run both implementations parallel.

HOPE for someone - something I shared might be a idea to take and stimulates or thinking too.  Or you spot a problem and point it out.

MJ

Maybe I forgot to mention: that both system implementation are designed to trade multiple Pairs at the same time - basically as many as you define.

(Note for someone who thinks manual trading is always better:

if one trades 8 Pairs at the same time you have to assess 16 Risk potions(SHORT and LONG) for each TF_group having 4 TF_groups one would have to keep track of 64 Risk assessments not to mention all the different Stochastic lines per TF_group. AND additionally keep track at about each Trade on which TF_group it is actually trading just to mention a few reason -- of course one can always just stick to 1 or 2 pairs ... but there are some god points in automatizing....)

--- 帖子 #1091 ---
Lubo good to see you working on the indicator.

not sure what you do not understand about the cross.

I try to explain simply what I mean:

Let's just use a SHORT Risk assessment as example:

You switch on your PC and start your indicator:

you check 5 things:

EASY: SHORT_PriceLine_above_76_4_OR_below  _23_6

EASY: SHORT_Stoch_Main_below_80

EASY: SHORT_Stoch_Filter_below_23_6

PROBLEM:

SHORT_Stoch_Main_crossed_below_Stoch_HighFrame

SHORT_OriginLine_crossed_below_76_4

Tell me how do you know if the OriginLine has crossed below 76.4% ?

You may say it the easy way: well if the Previous_OriginLine was above or at 76.4% and the next (LastClosed Candle) is below 76.4% it has crossed.

This is True (if I remember correctly skyline did something like that) and I do it also.

But it is just the half truth: look at Spuds picture below about the much later entry - this will happen (maybe in a slightly faster way) with using the M1 filter most of the time.

The cross could have happened at any time before the entry ...  It could have happened already before you switched on your PC. How do you know it has happened ???

Hope this clears a bit about the Problem of the crossing - it is mainly a problem because it must not happen simultaneously with our Trade enter (in fact it will properly not  happen often simultaneously because of the other assessments)

Hope this helps a bit.

--- 帖子 #1092 ---
Think of the price line and 14,3,3 much like a %K and %D..or almost any oscillator or moving avaerage with 2 lines.  Strong moves come when the lines split apart and then they eventually snap back together.

The problem with a 100,3,3 line that is responding quickly with the 14,3,3 line is that it usually is a weak situation.  The ideal situation, is that the 14,3,3 pulls away from the price line and heads for say, oversold.  Then the price line moves and follows it down.  That means we have travelled in a very strong down move.

If you look at good escalator moves in a down trend, you'll see this move.  In the strict system, I'm trying to use this split as a good down move.  We simply repeat this split through the time frames...in otherwords we are trying to avoid the snap back and take advantage of the stochastic placement that gives us the strongest move (reliably).  However, if you look back at M5 say from M30 and we are in a down trend you will likely see the 14,3,3 sticking in an oversold position and the M5 price line falling.

I don't want to confuse issues too much, so I'll leave it at that as to why we are using the split of the Origin and Price Line to enter a trade.

--- 帖子 #1093 ---
Well, i understand what u mean.

In my indi there is not this problem, all bar are indipendent:
Price:
- price above 76.4 & price  < price prev : color red

- price below 23.6 & price  < price prev : color green
Origin:
- origin below 76.4  & < origin prev : color red

- origin above 23.6 & > origin prev : color green
Stoch Cross:
- stoch cross1 < 20 & stoch cross1 < stoch cross2 & stoch cross1 < stoch cross1 prev : color red
- stoch cross1 > 20 & stoch cross1 > stoch cross2 & stoch cross1 > stoch cross1 prev : color green
Filter
filter < 23.6 : color red

filter > 76.4 : color green

When this combinations aren't meet : color neutral.

that's all!

Lubo.

This is an early entry. If your mental stop loss is set at the peak (as shown) +10 pips you'd remain in this trade. You stay in until you are positive pips or you reach the mental stop and there is no hope on M5 and/or M15.

Have we made pips? No.

Is there any signal for long? No.

Did we hit the mental stop? No.

Stay put. If the trade isn't to your liking set tp to 0 pips and either wait until we hit a condition that takes us out or you get out unscathed.

This isn't a pretty trade but M15 gives us all the reason to ride this out.

--- 帖子 #1111 ---
Ok, let me simplify this....

The chart below identifies the 5 last most obvious, and most reliable trade entries today. I am only looking at the Origin line crossing above 23.6 or below 76.4 and the Price Line with the Origin line. Whether we enter these trades depends on 3 other criteria.....our M5/M15 cross, our M1 filter, and our M5 cross 20/80. Again, this is the pickiest of picky trade entry situations. The 3 other criteria are there to confirm the "off peak" trade developed by the Origin Line and the Price Line.

So, the first criteria of money management is met that we want to know that our entry will be successful (as sure as we can be).

The next criteria is that we do not want to set our hard stops where our friendly broker can spike us out. Ideally, price will not draw down against us, but it will from time to time. We want a mental stop 10 pips from our peak. Our peak is the lowest or highest spot...we are always trading "off the peak".

We set an emergency stop 50-100 pips away from our entry...this is a hard stop. Our mental stop is 10 pips plus the peak,,this is a soft stop..one that does not exist other than in our brain. The red horizontal lines represent our mental stop. Please note that we never crossed the red line.

Each possible entry has a 15 PIP green line profit scale from entry to +5,+10 and +15 pips. Notice we are 100% on 15 pips. Notice how many times 5 pips is hit vs 15 pips. Notice how easy it was to hit within this 15 pip profit scale...this is profit (less 2 pip spread on entry and exit). Our final criteria is take the pips when you get them.

This is why I preach 20 pips per day. You don't need to chase trends or exit signals. This is 5 possible trades netting 75 pips in 12 hours. If you miss 2 entries...it is 45 pips. If you miss 4 entries it is 15 pips. Put your dollars in PIP value not chasing large numbers of pips. At $10 a pip this is $750 in 12 hours.

So here is how you manage your money:

1. Start trading with $0 per pip and learn to identify these entries. Demo trade the entries until you can win 80%....that means you don't hit the mental stop 8 of 10 trades. Track how many times you hit 5, 10 and 15 pip gains (net). Analyze why you failed...I will bet 80% of failures come from too early an entry.

2. Start trading with $1 a pip and target 20 pips a day. By now you should have no problem seeing the entries. Trade for 5 pips a trade...trade a smuch as you can. You will make more than 20 pips a day...but never think you are trading for more than 20 pips a day...rejoice that you set out to make 20 pips if you make 100 pips. As you succeed raise yourself to target 10 and 15 pips...but never be afraid you will hurt ypur ego if you jump out at 5 pips.

3. Every time you make more than 20 pips a day...you "bank" the rest. So if you make 80 pips in a day you bank 60 pips. This bank of pips covers any losses you suffer. Keep doing this until you make $5,000 at 20 pips a day. If your good it will take you 250 trade days at 20 pips a trade day If you want to speed it up use 50% of your banked pips to add to your $5,000 total.

4. When you have finally mastered the dicipline to do this (wax on, wax off...wax on, wax off)...then either trade a real account or trade $2 a pip and work your way up in $5,000 intervals. By now you are printing your own pay cheque and know what you are doing....and 20 pips a day gives you a life! That is the most important thing!!!!

That's it. That's my lecture on money management. I know that 99% of people who read it will ignore it. This is how you make an income you can rely on from trading. It is simple and unfortunately you won't have 200 pip trades to brag about...but you will make money this way and you will control it.

--- 帖子 #1169 ---
This is a really good question. I've been trying to figure this out myself.

--- 帖子 #1170 ---
This is where you need MTF.  However, it is far more likely for Origin to rebound to price, rather than Price to fall to the Origin.

Of course, there are always exceptions.  The most obvious is if the Origin stays in the oversold (below 23.6).  This will likely draw the price down.  Hence you want a breakout of the overmarket to trade the Origin back to price.  In cases where the Origin falls away from price to below 23.6, I'd be far more tempted to ride out the Origin below the 23.6, 20 or 15 to catch the oversold dive...if price does fall.

In general, the Origin cycles away from price line and back up to price line (remember smaller stochs oscillate faster)...as the top range weakens, price will start to come down with each move of the origin until it is so weak it follows the origin down or collapses and drops to the origin.

Eventually the price is going to move...our earlier time frames should give us a heads up when this is going to happen.

--- 帖子 #1184 ---
I want to take a step back to answer the question, why we enter a trade when the Price Line is above 76.4 and the Origin line goes below 76.4...or when the PL is below 23.6 and the OL is above 23.6.

The chart below demonstrates this. Each red line represents a point where the OL crossed 23.6 or 76.4 with the PL in the proper place.

The mental (not fixed) stop loss is 10 pips off our peak. The profit is 10 pips.

Each solid thick red line represents an entry that never hit the mental stop.

The dashed red lines represent where we made 10 pips profit and exited, some trades share the same exit.

The blue lines represent where we hit our mental stop and had to make a decision (more details follow).

There are 11 trades in 24 hours here and there is no reason why all 11 trades would not have been traded successfully for 10 pips.

If you study each trade in detail you will see what combinations support each trade.

This is on the M5. Now, let us look at something a little more interesting in details.

--- 帖子 #1185 ---
The chart below is details on a few of these trades. What you should notice is the relationship to the dashed red line representing where we made +10 pips and the peaking of the Origin Line..and/or the crossing of the Origin line relative to 23.6 or 76.4.

This is more of an "...isn't that interesting" correlation but it does show you how you could exit yourself out of a trade using the Origin Line and being relativel safe about it. You either take 10 pips or exit on the Origin Line crossing 23.6 or 76.4....or exit off the peak when the Origin Line changes direction.

This isn't a change from anything we have been talking about. What I'm showing you is the broad view of what is happening in our trade as the risk levels change. By flipping time frames we can extend our Origin Line and know whether to continue or not....you'll see the same correlations all the way through and the Origin Line spiking out or crossing a fib.

--- 帖子 #1187 ---
Here is the detail where our entries hit a our mental stop. We crossed our mental stop by 2 pips on the candle close...is that enough to exit?

This is where M1 comes into play(see insert)...notice how it is breaking out 1 minute after our mental stop is hit. The exact same principles of our entry into the M5 trade exist on the M1. If you were just using the M1 filter you would see this rising and why would you exit? (If M1 is diving your out).

Now...if the M1 stayed in the oversold and we dipped again, I'd be a lot quicker on the trigger. However, this is where M15 comes into play....is M15 moving off a peak? If it is, I'd stay in even if we don't have a signal for an M15 long yet, but we have passed a peak. For the record, M15 is coming off a peak in the oversold area....so with M1 and M15 we don't have to exit on the mental stop.

There is no doubt this is a tricky area of a trade...whether to ride out the bounce and possibly get caught in an oversold market or take a loss. If you take the loss.....you'd still make 40-50 pips for the day....and our target is 20 pips...right? The M1 here is our saving grace and the fact we closed only 2 pips by our mental stop. Deciding your exit based on simple patterns like this go far into making you a more efficient trader.

--- 帖子 #1188 ---
I'm just showing you can take the safest trades..be picky and still make good pips in a day. This is the safest way to trade stochastics when the PL is in the overmarket and the OL is leaving the over market.

Also, just trying to give a better overview of where we should be trading when we are entering a trade and where we are in the combination world on these trades. This is not the only way...it is the safest way.

--- 帖子 #1193 ---
You may notice we get a lot of "double" entry opportunity with one entry too early and the real entry following a little later with a slightly higher peak.  Usually this doesn't hit the mental stop too often...unles we are way early.  One way to use this is to be ultra cautious on the first entry (as it may be the only entry) and play a straight drop..any sign of reversal or increase in risk and start looking for a breakeven exit...or you may get a new entry before that which can solidify staying in.

Practice and watching M5, M1 and M15 you'll start to get the feel of how these are acting and if there is going to be some problems.  Just watching how fast price reacts to M1 filter moves can give good insight into if we are a little early or not.

I suggest 76.3 and 23.6...but no reason you can't move those out to create more filter room say..20/80 or even 15/85...or even 90/10 and the M5 trigger.  Still, with watching the stiochs move is by far the best advantage you have.

--- 帖子 #1195 ---
Here's a comparison of the early entry versus the good entry on JD's posting. The chart on the left is the early entry and the chart on the right, the good entry a little later.

Notice our M5's are almost identical.

The M15 crossover and filter look almost identical too. But look at the M15's Price and Origin lines. The M15 on the early entry is a marginal short given that if it goes short the price line hasn't risen above 76.4. The only way we can get M15 and M30 to carry over from M5 short entry and go escalator down is with an M15 climb (and M30 climb) first. Look at the M15 and M30 on the good entry...here we can keep our short entry going through the time frames and possible line up an escalator down. No possibility in the early entry, possibility in the good entry.

You can clearly see here which entry is safer and where patience pays off.

This is what I mean about being picky about your trades. If we wait for our trades to give us the most possibility for long term success (as an escalator down would be)...then it means our short term trades success is amplified a hundred times.

If you are mechanical about this and trade every trade on set conditions, it is an inefficient process but you do not have to watch it. If you watch what is happening and seek out the optimum targets then sniping 20 Pips isn't to hard.

I showed you previously how M5 lines up with a multitude of opportunity and how just using the single M5 with Price Line and Origin Line can be extremely successful. But it is not perfect! When you incorporate the multiple time frames, the combination rules and look for the rollover from M5 to M15 to M30 to H1 being a possible development, our trade entries get very succesful. In other words, if you can can get a M5 entry with an M15 entry forming or even happening at the same time, there's far more success than just using M5.

Put value into pips for the trades that line up better and take value out of the pips for weak trades. We won'yt always have the second entry set-up so put small lots sizes on the simple but weak entries. When things are lining up and much stronger...risk more lots into your pips. Statistically you will be much further ahead as the weaker trades will lose more than the stronger trades.

For example if we risk $1 a pip on every M5 entry, but say double or triple up when we have a corresponding M5 and M15 entry, and say triple up when we have a corresponding M5,M15 and M30 entry..then you take advantage of the strength of the trade.....play for 10 pips...get out. If you have a strong triple entry you might put 1 LOT to a trend (ride the escalator down) and 1 lot for 10 pips...challenge yourself to come out no worse than breakeven. You can play many different $$ entry combinations to get your pips for the day. Play for more $$ and less pips if you like, for example. Just be picky on your trades.

--- 帖子 #1199 ---
I have spent some time tinkering with the mechanicals.  My dilema was formulating a good balance between profits and stops, while keeping the mechanical system simple and low risk.  Obvious measure of running without any stop loss and using money management to rebound from a losing trade seemed one choice, but chasing an 80 pip draw down for a 10 pip gain seemed a little crazy.

I made some minor changes to the stochastic levels and set some simpler rules for entry based on the 100,3,3 Price Line and the 14,3,3 Origin Line.  This I hoped would help our programmers for back testing and more so to help us indentify early trades in an easier manner.

The problem with fixed profit targets is that stochastics don't move to the exact range of the price.  In other words a 50% rise in stochastics may only result in a 2 pip price rise.  We get around this somewhat with our Price Line, it better mimics price, but this too can be off the mark in the over markets if range is changing.  So, defining fixed targets becomes a statistical game of keeping wins ahead of losses.

So, I wanted to develop a little more balance to the system by keeping the stop loss and profits more centered within a range.  To do that, I decided to go with using rules within the price chart.

Well lo and behold while I'm in the midst of drawing charts up does someone go and post a similar idea.  I originally set my price targets in 10 pip intervals, but stretching them to the 25 pip intervals seemed to result in better balance and as such I decided to borrow that idea and apply it to our mechanicals.

Again, nothing really new here with the stochastics but we are tinkering a bit to make the mechanicals more efficient and the system a little easier to use.

M5 Chart

Set stochastics levels at 16.4, 20 and 23.6  this band between 16.4 and 23.6 represents our "floor"

Set stochastics levels at 76.4, 80 and 83.6  this band between 76.4 and 83.6 represents our "ceiling"

Stochastics are Price Line 100,3,3 and Origin Line 14,3,3

We trade "off the peak".  This means that in a long trade as an example:

1.  The Peak is defined as the lowest candle and Price Line stochatic point just prior to our entry.  Just prior means...say no more than 5 candles back.

2.  The Origin Line and Price Line must be below the floor when the peak is created.

3.  The Price Line must remain below the floor (in the basement) at point of entry.

4.  The Point of Entry is defined when the Origin Line crosses 16.4, 20 and/or 23.6.  Using 16.4 is more aggressive than 23.6 but not overly aggressive, you can choose your level of entry.

Profits and Losses

We set our price grid on our price chart at every 25 pips...so 00,25,50 and 75..simple enough.

Exit profit is when our price hits the the next price grid line.  So if we enter at 2745...our exit is not 2750 but 2775.  If we enter at 2751, our exit is not 2775 but 2800.

Stops are the opposite....we stop at the next grid line below our entry.  So if we enter at 2745...or stop is not 2725 but 2700.   If we enter at 2751, our stop is not 2750 but 2725.

Just to show you how balanced this profit and loss is, here are the results for the last 16 trades (gross pips without spread):

+41, +30, +34, +32, +33, +33, +30, +36, +38, -31, +39, -38, -47, +29, +29

Total: +318 Pips in 31 hours

I figured the balance between profit and loss made this interesting enough to post.  Please don't use real $$ on it yet, it may need some refining and may have some hidden issues not yet exposed.  Hopefully a few of you will play with it so we can put it to the test.

--- 帖子 #1206 ---
Looking at the combinations we can break the trend. A little refinement on the system using the combinations.

We miss two false entries from M1 filter early in the trend, and catch a good 10 pips on a good combo entry. Notice that in the middle of the false and good entries is a peak...but that peak is lower than the one where are false entries were (can't see it here). The good entry has a new peak that is higher.

Notice how the M1 filter, crossover and x80 delayed the entry on the good trade by about 5 mins. We are close enough to the peak, form where the Origin Line crossed.

I adjusted the target profit/stop grid to go back to the original 10 pips. This in part is the effect of delay from combo signals. If you check the combinations at the 10 pip taret this is where we can decide to exit or extend it to 15, 20 or 25...but if we bounce back say from 14 to to 10 we should exit. Go for the straight run for extra pips. I've set the grid off from the entry price, not the round numbers. The stop is tightened but you'll need to view the combos and time-frames to decide to stay or exit. The stop is tightened because there are few occurances where it is hit, vs wins, and where it is not obvious by looking at the time frames it would be a good idea to exit.

It isn't mechanical anymore, but I think with this combo you'll find a good slew of winners and positive pips. As well this deals with trends and ranges nicely. Still be a few losers in the mix. Still refining for better TP/stops to help make this easier.

--- 帖子 #1216 ---
The filter and crosses "can" delay the entry.  These aren't new systems, just different ways to use the tools at hand.  The last description was simply one form that can be used, for those that may struggle identifying trades and need a more b&w kind of approach.

I do believe though we can simplify what constitutes a safe entry, what things we need confirmation un to make it a safe entry and where we can set stops an profits to make our trade more efficient.

For example a simple e-mail/alarm indicator for when our PL and and OL are above 76.4 or below 23.6 would allow traders not to watch the screen all day.

Determiing a profit and stop window allows for traders to walk away.

The remainder of say, setting up an escalator trade can only be done watching the trade unfold.

The R0 to R100 is a checklist of what to look for in a trade.

NOW: if you would choose without simplified for a mechanical system:

How would you describe the best SHORT ENTRY.

I came up with such:

* ESSENTIALS

M5: PriceLine_M5, OrigLine_M5 Stoch_M5 (14,1,1), Rope_M5 (18 Stoch)

M15: OriginLine_M15* PEAKED all together above PeakLevel same time (PossibleTrade Initial Trigger) e.g 90%

PriceLine_M5, OrigLine_M5, Stoch_M5 (14,1,1), Rope_M5

* PriceLine_M5 stayed above: its Defined Level e.g 80%

* OriginLine_M5 crossed below and stayed below: its Defined LevelLevel e.g: 76.4%

* Stoch_M5 (14,1,1) below OriginLine_15

* Stoch_M5 (14,1,1) below defined distant to OriginLine_M5 -- measures also a bit the strength of the expected movement

* Rope_M5 Order_Low_to_High: meaning close together or orderly spread: no net

Trade will only be executed if all Essentials are met

* Confirmation_RISK= 11

M15: PriceLine_M15, OriginLine_M15        (each counting 3 more important)

M30: PriceLine_M30, OriginLine_M30        (each counting 2 less important)

M1: Filter_M1                                              (counting 1 least important)* PriceLine_M15 above defined Level. e.g 76.4%* OriginLine_M15 above defined Level. e.g 76.4%* PriceLine_M30 above defined Level. e.g 76.4%* OriginLine_M30 above defined Level. e.g 76.4%* Filter_M1 below below defined Level. e.g 23.6%           (does the filter still make sense with the Rope ? )

Trades will be executed only when ESSENTIALS are met -

UnitSize will be reduced base on Confirmation_RISK

* e.g Confirmation_RISK 11 - will be using just 5% of the normal Unitsize

Do you have any comments, improvement ideas - did I cover most of the MTF Stochastic ?

waiting patently for your comments

MJ

--- 帖子 #1219 ---
This is how I would define a short entry.

The essential checklist for a safe short entry:

Check 1 (M5 Chart – Pending Trade Warning):
Price Line (100,3,3) must have peaked above 76.4
“Peaked” means we do not have a higher PL stochastic level previous to our current PL stochastic level since the PL crossed 76.4 (up)
Origin Line (14,3,3) crosses 76.4 (down)
The OL must cross down from above 76.4 after our Peak

Check 2 (M5/M15 Stochastic Crossover):
M5 stochastic (14,1,1) must cross (down) below the M15 stochastic either before or at point of entry and stay below the M15 at point of entry.

Check 3 (M5 below 80):
M5 (14,1,1) must be below 80 at point of entry
This is not the same as the Origin Line (14,3,3) below 76.4 as this is the (14,1,1) stochastic below 80.

Check 4 (M1 Filter – Point of Entry):
M1 (14,3,3) must be below 23.6. When Checks 1-3 are true, enter at first close of M1 where the M1 filter is true.

Trading:
Progress through the time frames looking for the same checklist completion or that the longer time frames are moving in a way that the checklist can be completed. Use a large hard stop and peak plus 10 mental stop. Target for set pips or exit when the checklist will not be fulfilled in a larger time frame….or cannot be supported in a lesser time frame. Trade the time frame that supports the checklist.

Mechanical Trading:
Check 1 is the main entry point (use 83.6, 80 or 76.4) of OL cross for entry. The peak, OL and PL must be above 83.6. Look to M1 Filter (Check 4) to focus entry point. Use Check 2 and 3 to confirm entry for a more conservative approach.
Set a grid at even 10’s, 20’s or 25’s of price chart, exit/or stop on second grid line reached from point of entry. Exception is starting on the grid, then exit/stop on next grid line.
Only enter 1 trade where PL is above 83.6. Cannot enter a new trade until PL falls below 76.4 and rises above 83.6 (this protects against trends in an over market condition).

Safety Belt:
To ensure you are trading off the peak, you can wait for the Price Line to dip close to the 83.6 line so long as there is a higher price line point prior to this. You will need the Origin Line to be separated from the Price Line to some degree, or appear they are separating at point of entry. Use M1 Filter and remainder of checklist to support an entry this way. This is a late entry and as such you should tighten your target profit or be alert to what other time frames are doing. And follow the other time frame checklists from here on. This works better entering on M15 rather than M5 as it will give you more possible opportunity for pips that exist in a wider ranged price market. If you are fluent in using the multiple time frames, this is a very safe method for entry on M5 as log as you are targeting an escalator or sniping pips.

Hi chehab,

Each column represents the combination as according to the  Spud rules, ie for example:
M5 column:

Price set to TF 5

Origin set to TF 5

cross1 set to TF 5

cross2 set to TFf 15

filter set to TF 1
M15 column:

Price set to TF 15

Origin set to TF 15

cross1 set to TF 15

cross2 set to TFf 30

filter set to TF 5

an so on fo the other column.

These are the combinations that had already described in a previous post:

Price:
- price above 76.4 & price  < price prev : color red

- price below 23.6 & price  < price prev : color green
Origin:
- origin below 76.4  & < origin prev : color red

- origin above 23.6 & > origin prev : color green
Stoch Cross:
- stoch cross1 < 20 & stoch cross1 < stoch cross2 & stoch cross1 < stoch cross1 prev : color red
- stoch cross1 > 20 & stoch cross1 > stoch cross2 & stoch cross1 > stoch cross1 prev : color green
Filter
filter < 23.6 : color red

filter > 76.4 : color green

When this combinations aren't meet : color neutral.

--- 帖子 #1266 ---
I might have a suggestion for everyone.

I used to trade the e-mini (mini dow) before coming over to the forex.

One of the indicators that I used on the mini-dow was the

"Guppy Multiple Moving Averages" made popular by Daryl Guppy in

Australia.

The set-up is this:

3 ema blue      Short term moving averages/short term investers

5 ema blue

8 ema blue

10 ema blue

12 ema blue

15 ema blue

30 ema red      Long term moving averages/long term investers

35 ema red

40 ema red

45 ema red

50 ema red

60 ema red

These moving averages will determine the trend.  Short term moving

averages = short term investers.  Long term moving averages = long

term investers.  Don't go against the short term and long term trends.

You need to scan them up on your platform and watch them for awhile.

They are very accurate and using Spuds stoch's settings it seems very

accurate to me.  Just a suggestion for everyone.  Hope it helps!

snarlyjack

--- 帖子 #1275 ---
This is my first post of the thread after reading through everything, trying it out in live trading, and actually finding merit to the system.  In my experience most people start threads that have really had no success at all in trading, but play themselves off as experts.  It is apparent to me that Spud really does know his stuff, so I give him mad props.

So far I am 3/3 for this week trading EURUSD, but I do not use Stochs all by themselves.  I have simply tried utilizing the MTF stochs to better pinpoint my entries and to determine exits.  I have posted a picture of my trading setup just for curiousity's sake only.  I encourage everyone to take Spud's knowledge and turn it into something that works for you.  I believe that is what he is trying to encourage as well.

One of the best things we all can do to become better traders is to keep a journal of all our trades.  My humble suggestion for everyone is to start grading the trades you place so you know how you are actually doing.  The two hardest things to do are 1) remain patient and stay in a trade when the signals tell you to do so 2) exit a trade and admit you are wrong.  Grading your trades will tell you how you are faring in these regards.

Grading your trade

I like to grade all my trades as suggested by Dr. Alexander Elder.  He grades based off channels, but I grade my own trades based off the high/low range of pips from my entry to the best possible exit.  I have graded my three trades from this week below.  As you will see sometimes a 10 pip trade is an A trade, while a 20 pip trade may only rate a C.

Grading System

Capture more than 30% of available pips = A

Capture between 20-30% of pips = B

Capture between 10-20% of pips = C

Capture less than 10% of pips = D

Trade 1

S eurusd @ 1.2922     Exit @ 1.2912     +10 pips

Range: 1.2925 - 1.2907                     = 18 pips

10/18 = .5555 or 56%

Grade: A

Trade 2
B eurusd @ 1.2874      Exit @ 1.2896     +22 pips

Range: 1.2867 - 1.3000                       =133 pips

22/133 = .1654 or 17%

Grade: C

As you can see I was far too impatient on trade 2 as I missed a boatload of pips.  The trend was in my favor and the escalator was in motion.  Still a C is passing and acceptable for now.  Just a lesson to be learned along the way.

Hope the grading system helps some other traders, and thanks to Spud for all the time he has taken outlining this information for free!

--- 帖子 #1284 ---
hi sarah2002, it's ok to have high dreams and wishes as all of us. BUT ...

99% safe trades ( one Entry a day 10 pip TP - assuming 250 trading days a year)

* In  2 years you would have had: 500 Trades - 495 Trades Winner each 10 PIPS: 495 * 10 PIPs = 4950 PIPs

- 5 Trades Looser (setting StopLoss 990 PIPs away):  5 * 990 PIPs  = 4950 PIPs
So the real Question is: Can you do that:

500 Trades TakeProfit 10 PIPs, StopLoss 990 Pips: do you have just 5 looser? Maybe but ?

Some other thoughts: even if you have in the end just 5 looser !! you MUST enter a new trade each day  -- Do you have enough Margin to do that and make a meaningful Profit by 10 PIPs TakeProfit setting?

No offence sarah2002 - I think 99% safe trades (one each day) is not realistic - except you don't trade at all. http://www.forexfactory.com/images/icons/icon12.gif

But we all try to get closer to that.

wish all of us good trading.

MJ

Even if we could achieve this success rate there are at least 2 major problem I see:

- NOT enough margin (for meaningful Profit) in a time where a couple of trades turn against us (by 990 PIPs StopLoss setting) to enter each day a new trade.

- What about if we have the five first trade the StopLoss of 990 Pips hit ?

- this leaves us only with setting the Stop Losss much closer - and than it is even harder to achieve such success rate 99 % safe trade.

There are still some other thoughts: if in case we make sometimes more then 10 PIPs profit ? would be a very positive influence. etc.......

What is the optimal StopLoss setting to win???

--- 帖子 #1288 ---
Heres a couple more examples of the divergence in action but also shows another filter I've been using whereby instead of entering right on the close of the signal candle, waiting until the low is broken... This filters out a few bad trades too.

Particularly those annoying ones that reverse right on entry and never even bring you into profit like the first one.

We had the signal and normal procedure would be to enter straight away but waiting to make sure the low gets broken would of kept us out of this bad trade.

You might also notice the hidden divergence straight after this bad entry where by the price makes a slightly Higher low but the %K makes a much much lower low - this is a bullish signal.

the examples I showed above were all the same type where for example price makes a higher high (swing high) but the stoch makes a lower high - this is bearish Divergence

Or where price makes alower low but the stock makes a higher low - Bullish divergence

Then thers Hidden divergence but I wont go into that you can read about it if you want to at the link I posted above

--- 帖子 #1295 ---
Well it worked in a sense that it wasnt there so stopped me looking for trades - When it did exist there was usually a small but profitable bounce until it hit the top and had the big bounce....

on the other hand there was also lots of hidden divergence that played well with elasticity trades going WITH the trend - this is where for example for a bullish hidden divergence the price makes a HIGHER LOW butt he stoch make a much LOWER LOW (chart below)

its slightly confusing at first but very easy to getthe hang of theres only 4 divergence signals

1- Price HH - Stoch LH - Bearish (normal divergence)

2- Price LL - Stoch HL - Bullish (normal divergence)

3-Price HL - Stoch LL - Bullish (Hidden divergence)

4 -Price LH - Stoch HH - Bearish (Hidden Divergence)

It wasnt my intension to turn this thread into a divergence lesson sorry Spud just wanted to throw some ideas out there but maybe we can build something around this im not sure

--- 帖子 #1317 ---
hi sarah2002,

I was also thinking a little bit about that.  As had to program all my indicators (not so many at the moment) myself I also did the Stochastic one.
Formula

First the %K(fast) line is calculated, as with the Fast Stochastics. (This line is not shown in the graph.)

*   The %K(fast) line is defined as follows:

%K(fast) = (CP - Ln) / (Hn - Ln) * 100

where CP = Latest Closing Price, n = the number of periods, Ln = the Lowest bid price  over the last n periods, and Hn = the Highest ask price over the last n periods.

Then:

%K(full) = m1-period simple moving average of the %K(fast) line

%D(full) = M2-period simple moving average of the %K(full) line

Parameters

The Full Stochastics has three parameters:

* n specifies the number of periods to use when calculating the initial %K(fast).

* m1 specifies the number of periods over which the %K(full) line is to be smoothed.

* m2 specifies the number of periods used to calculate the %D line.
I do not have the time right now (too busy with my new bot) to really think it through if we can get from that the results you are looking for -- maybe -- maybe not.

Maybe the formula is a help for some of you to think that through.

MJ
