--- 帖子 #1322 ---
I would consider the following a tool, to use in conjunction with the Combination Rules, Escalator to Pips, Sonic Indicator, or anything else you like.

I've included the templates below, as the setup is quite cumbersome for MT4 newbies. I'll explain what is in the Dynamik, but not how to set it up on MT4....use the templates!

Spud's Dynamik is used to follow momentum, trend and trend changes. there are 4 key components:

1. Price Chart - MacD 12,26,9

Trend change is indicated when the (red) bars cross the (yellow) moving average line.

Long Term Momentum is measured by the MacD values of the highs and lows for the corresponding segments (see chart below). For example, progressive lower valued "short" peaks indicate a longer long trend if the "long" peaks are higher in value. (read more on MacD in Google)

Short Term Momentum is measured from the bars...bars increasing in length mean sustained momentum, bars shortening mean weakening momentum.

2. Chart 2 - Stochastics Scale

We bring in the stochastics but use neither the %K or %D...what we simply want is the stochastics to lock in the 80/20 % scale for us.

3. Chart 2 - MACD-Colored_v102 5,13,1

This is a slighty modified MacD indicator. The only line we use is the moving average line (yellow). However, we are using the other hidden elements of the MAcD in a different way. These elements are the tri-signal average lines calculated from the MacD, and the "shift" of the MacD scale within our stochastic scale. I will go into more detail on the "shift" later. We can also use this as a momentum tool, when (yellow) moving average line peaks the price is exhausted in that direction. We camn also incompass the (yellow) moving average for "off-peak" trading when it peaks above 80 and below 20.

4. Chart 2 - Tri-Signal Moving Averages MA(2),(3),(4)

This is our confirmation tool for trend changes. The moving averages signal when MA(2) and MA(4) converge and cross. When and where this happens is the most important factor.

When it happens after a cross of the (yellow) moving average line

When it happens at the peak of the (yellow) moving average line

In all cases, this convergence must correspond to our first MacD (on the price chart) when the bars cross the moving average. This may happen at the same time, just before or just after.

Below is a quick look at the chart and I'll break it down into detail in the following posts.

--- 帖子 #1323 ---
Below are examples of the (red) bars crossing the (yellow) MA of our MacD where the yellow arrows point. We can also see on our price chart the corresponding price moves. This is called our Dynamik Cross.

The vertical lines represent our trend change area. This area is denoted by where we get our Dynamik Cross and the Tri-Signal Convergence Cross on our other chart (not shown).

I messed up with the graphic on the 3rd cross, it should be the next bar. But picking tat as a cross isn't wrong...just early and predictive.

I'm not going to explain using this for momentum. There is a wealth of infomation on MacD as a momentum indicator with the settings of 12,26,9...I strongly suggest you read and understand that...just google MacD Momentum. I believe the momentum aspect is fairly obvious.

Of course using this indicator alone is not enough. Although it can be extremely acurate alone, it is also prone to many false signals. So as always we need to weed out those false signals as best we can without impacting the good signals.

--- 帖子 #1324 ---
So the first one was easy....this is a little more complicated...but is really easy once you get the hang of it.

Let's talk about this chart for a while because there are many things going on all at once. We have to learn to read this chart to fully appreciate it everything it tells us.

If you ever scrolled through a MacD chart you know that the scale shifts when price breaks the scale (range) boundaries. This shift is an extremely important tool for filtering out price moves in the over bought/sold markets. You need to be aware of this shift because it greatly affects any backtesting you do. You cannot look at MacD on this chart statically, you will have to scroll forward and watch for shifts of the (yellow) MacD MA. We are only worried about the "present" location and not the past of the MAcD MA.

This shift is why we have incoporated the stochastic 100% scale. This makes it far easier to see the over bought/sold conditions occurring beacuse MacD cannot exceed our scale and therefore must shift within our scale.

THE ONLY THING YOU NEED TO KNOW NOW IS THAT THE "SHIFT" OCCURS AND IF BACKTESTING YOU MUST ACCOUNT FOR THIS SHIFT.

So let's leave the shift behind for another rainy day and look at to what signals trend change.

The vertical lines correspond to my previous chart post..here we just have the green and blue vertical lines. These lines represnt the fuzzy area of our trend change....I call them Dynamik Transition Zones. They simply mark when we get our first signal from or Dynamik Cross and then mark where our Tri-Signal MA's converge and cross. That's it.

So, the Dynamik Transition Zone is the time between our Dynamik Cross and latest Tri-Signal Convergence Cross. This can be simultaneous or spread out....but it must happen or we won't have a trend change. We generally want it to happen as close together as possible.

The other dynamic of our Dynamik Transition Zone is where the Tri-Signal Convergence Cross occurs. There are really only two positions we want...the move across our (yellow) MAcD MA or one that occurs at a MacD MA peak. Remember we only care about the one near to our Dynamik Cross, the rest don't matter. This location of our Tri-Signal Convergence Cross is called our Dynamik Signal.

So what we want to establish is our Dynamik Transition Zone which is made up of our:

Dynamik Cross

Dynamik Signal

Just burn this chart below in your head.

Obviously we won't see a transition zone until it happens. But as such we have three points of entry we can confirm with whatever else we use to enter a trade. The first and earliest would be to receive only a Dynamik Cross or Dynamik Signal...this is obviously the riskiest but may get you in earlier. The second is waiting for the Transition Zone to establish and trade at the point the zone is established. The third is to wait and trade after the transition zone. You can usually see things developing so when you use this tool, you'll find it much easier to time trades inreal time.

There are two more important details. The first is the peak. Trading off the MacD MA peaks on the Dynamic Filter is almost always a guarantee for a long trend...well as long as the trend allows. If you use this in combination with every thing else and whatever you use to enter then you will almost certainly have a good trade with the trend and have filtered out the over market killer. The important thing about trading off these peaks is waiting for our Transition Zone to get established and the "shift" to end (more on shift later).

The last detail is the MacD 0 line. If our Tri-Signals don't cross the 0 line our current trend stays true. They may ride the 0 line..or fuzzy around the 0 line...but no cross keeps our trend true. This is a very delayed indicator unfortunately, because we should be entering trades just before the cross of the 0 line to maximize our entry. However, with your other tools at hand you will learn to use this during your trade.

So, that's seems like a lot but in practice it is all actually very easy to understand and see.

Let's examine a trade with our Combination Rules and see how we do.

Chart time is 12/12 9:35 EurUsd and we have our first signal coming from our Dynamik Cross where the MacD on our price chart (red) has crossed the (black) MacD MA.

Everything else at this point is pretty much a no go for trade entry, but we do have some hopes we may get a long entry developing.

The second chart 10 mins later tells us everthing is a go or a Long trade. We have our Combination Rules met, we have a Dynamic Transition Zone established when we got the Dynamic Signal.

So, Long it is at 9:45 chart time (9:50 EST +7).

--- 帖子 #1329 ---
We are now just into our trade and something kinda cool is going to happen. We are going to witness the Dynamik Filter "shift".

Notice on the bottom chart the MAcD (black) line is all the way up near the top. Also see the MacD 0.00 line is well near the top as well.

In the second chart I will show you the "shift". You will see the 0.00 line come down as the MacD shifts in the upward trend. This is an easy play to follow in a trade and you can also see our MacD on the price chart is still in the long trend and our M1 filter will go into overbought.

The second chart goes to the end of the shift motion. So, you noticed price dropped. Eh? (Being Candian we say, "eh?" a lot). What don't you see here. You don't see our MAcD indicating any break in our Long Trend and look at how low our M15 stochastic is. You know what you are looking at.....this is M1 and M5 stochs coming down to get the M15 to bring it back up.

--- 帖子 #1330 ---
You have calculated the "1-period moving average" aka %k FAST.

To get SLOW %k all you need to do is take the average of the previous 3 periods of what you already calculated (%k fast.)

To get the SLOW %d you need to calculate the n period moving average of the SLOW %K.

Good luck with all that!

So let's jump to the exit. During that rade we had another shift, the MacD's kept us in our uptrend and basically there was nothing but follow the M15 stochastic up to the top peak where it now sits.

One thing to note is the The Dynamik Cross. You may think the cross happened earlier at Arrow 1...this is not a cross as our bars have reversed coming up above the MacD zero level..so these long bars have to shorten up now and fall below our MAcD MA as they do at Arrow 2.

You can also clearly see our Dynamik Siganl at the peak of the MacD that established our Transition Zone.

Oou Combinaion Rules..are clearly heading for a short...note how much longer we could stay in this trade and folow the trend and how it coincided with our M15 Stochastic.

All of this works together.

Just a feedback of my own process!

Well, after implementing the first BOT version of Spud's mechanical approach -  I went back to what Spud wrote about:

For my new 'highly configurable advanced entry BOT version 2'http://www.forexfactory.com/images/icons/icon12.gif I made nearly all parameters adjustable.

* All Stochastic settings are changeable as well the time of each Time Frame Level.

As it says, I'm still working mainly on the entry: for that I added a chart full of MTF conditions over 5 TimeFrame Levels (many conditions repeat themselves over the TF levels but I still kept each freely adjustable)*   I have at the moment 132 Risk Conditions (66 SHORT and 66 LONG) - it sounds more than it is if you calculate the Five Levels and for instance Direction pointing of the PriceLines and OriginLines you've got already 10

which I can include or not include in my Risk check.

Well - not absolutely free as some depend on others.

(my first BOT had many things not adjustable and just a small number of conditions)

*   On Level 1 one of the condition to be included is the Rope. ( I might extend that later easily to the other levels if I desire.)

*  I don't use our mechanical Filter Stoch (M1) anymore

*  I did not have yet a look if Spud's new 'dynamic MacD Filter' might be something worthy to include - still waiting to see what comes out of it ...

*   Each of the 132 Risk Conditions (66 SHORT and 66 LONG) I can designate to be:  ESSENTIAL  or CONFIRMATION.

For a valid New Entry all my ESSENTIAL Condition must be met, the CONFIRMATION Conditions I use for trade size adjustments.

*   A nice other notable feature is: Each Risk Condition can be prioritised by assigning a Count Value.

* I don't know yet for sure about exit. my rough thought now:

Define a second separate Exit Condition Map (which will properly overlap a lot with the Entry Conditions) and go the same way.

(for those interested: Just the risk check for one Level takes about 800 Lines code -- well this includes empty lines and quite some docs too)

--- 帖子 #1341 ---
Here's a trade with the Sonic Indicator, Dynamik and Combos....you can easily see how they all work together.

Trade signals start popping in the Transition Zone on the Dynamik. Depending how you want to enter, by the Combos, by the end of the transition zone at the Dynamik Cross...it is your choice. Also look how how the Sonic Indicator is showing us this trade by convergence and crossing the 76.4.

Take a good look at the square box on the Dynamik Filter chart. You will see this pattern many times for a great exit signal. The ultimate exit is where the red arrow points. See how the Tri-Signals and the MacD MA split apart..and the small peak prior to that where they come together as seen where the green arrow is. You will see this signal time and time again, a good one to post on the wall. As I said, this is a great exit confirmation.

If we wait...we get our M5 crossing up over the M15 to exit, or our Sonic breaking out from the oversold convergence.

You can see how our short trade ran the M15 nicely in one smooth move.

This is Nov 24 around 1:10 (EST +7) to 3:20. I decided I put Nov 24th to the test as there is a nice long trend with tons of false entries for the combos...so let's see how we do when we add the Dynamik.

Hi Spud,

I have been reading up on your post.  Good stuff, but by adding more and more indicators it makes it more confusing. I prefer the old stochastic method and let your mind get used to it, instead of adding filters, etc.  Just my 2c worth.

Everyone talks about making $$ in forex, but I have increasingly read about how many people get their trading platform frozen when placing trades or how profits have been eradicated, etc - methods used to ensure the profitable trader does not continue to be profitable because the dealer takes the other side of the trade.  Is there a dealer out there that is honest and reliable?

--- 帖子 #1354 ---
I post all the systems as different ways to view the same thing.  Some people are going to find it easier to use one than the other...but they are all based in the same "science".  Combinations, of indicators will/may help narrow down an entry and keep people out of trouble.

Re: brokers;  The largest danger to the small trader is setting fixed (small) stops.  All our stops are seen and when they clump together there is usually a spike to take them all out...but I didn't say that.

The brokers keep the spread...in the markets we are the winners and losers...for one of us to win, someone else is losing.  That is why you'll never find the perfect system or EA...it's a zero sum game winners=losers.

Brokers love traders, winners or losers.  They'd probably be happier if we won, as we'd trade more with them.

It's the same old myth about casinos cheating..casinos don't need to cheat..they have a guaranteed income built into every game based on the house advantage.....brokers make money whether we win or lose.  Both just make money with the money that passes through their hands.

I really don't find any one broker better than another...they all seem to have their issues and graces, just happening at different times.  For me, it is about customer service, access to my funds, etc. and being able to talk to real people and having a single contact that knows me.

I've never had a broker freeze my account for winning.  Some get a little testy at scalping, I just say bye-bye.

Well,  I don't really know why I get so involved with Spud's systems.

* But somehow I loved his presentations enough to believe it 'could really work out well' (but this has still to be proven for me ;-)

* The other thing I like a lot - there is enough infos here to play with the main concept in many different ways - which gives plenty of option for Money Management and other things.

The feeling of satisfaction !!

The new additional version of my Bot 3 -  is more or less ready for testing. (was much easier this time - as I could build on all the previous related stuff and had already most of the ideas in my mind)

It's huge, highly configurable and at a level it would be very difficult to maintain by manual  trading. (well manually has other great levels which the bot does not have like the 'brain indicator').

ayaz will be glade to hear.

* In this version I also extended my Fix TP option to 3 levels (each with possible multiple trades)

About Money Management: The Base UNIT Size is based on the result from one of my existing extended Money Management systems.

This is completely different than Spuds 20 PIPS a day plus Pips Bank.

Base UNIT Size calculation

at the new Bot 3 I have 72 Short and 72 Long possible Risk Checks - each check can have different count weight so to give certain Checks more importance than others if wanted.

Depending on what checks are included I calculate the highest possible Risk.

my FINAL Base UNIT Size is the: Base UNIT Size multiplied by a RISK_UnitsAdjustmentPercentage

(which in turn is calculated from the Actual Current Risk Percentage of the highest possible Risk.)

Based on this FINAL Base UNIT Size I split a trade in unlimited (3, 10 , 20) configurable multiple sub  trades

So a possible TP scenario could be like that:

* ESSENTIALS are met: I split a FINAL Base UNIT Size into 3 multiple sub  trades1 - TP 5 PIPS (50 % Units)

2 - TP 7 PIPS (30 % Units)

3 - TP 9 PIPS (20 % Units)

* ESSENTIALS + ESSENTIALS BONUS 1 are met: I split a FINAL Base UNIT Size into 3 multiple sub trades1 - TP 10 PIPS (50 % Units)

2 - TP 13 PIPS (30 % Units)

3 - TP 16 PIPS (20 % Units)* ESSENTIALS + ESSENTIALS BONUS 1 + ESSENTIALS BONUS 2 are met: I split a FINAL Base UNIT Size into 3 multiple sub trades (depending on the config this could be a Escalator to PIPs)1 - TP 15 PIPS (50 % Units)

2 - TP 25 PIPS (30 % Units)

3 - TP 40 PIPS (20 % Units)I will also do a Trailing SL or at least one to set Break Even for the higher TP.

So all together I feel satisfied with this concept .http://www.forexfactory.com/images/icons/icon7.gifhttp://www.forexfactory.com/images/icons/icon14.gif

Especially the MoneyManagement, TP and hundreds of configuration options.

Now - I think I will take some programming rest -- just check for stability and take care of the possible bugs (which by this huge code is quite expected)

And collect some new statistics.

If anyone is interested: I thing I shared a great deal of my system in this thread - and hope it inspires programmer as well as even none programmer to explore more of the possibilities.http://www.forexfactory.com/images/icons/icon12.gif

Basically I think - I more or less arrived in the implementation of MTF Stochastic into a fully automatized trading system.

(there might be small additions: have some ideas like including the angle of the rope etc but not in the immediate future)

And most of all: Prove if it is overall well profitable - and get live with it in about 3 month time --  otherwise just get rid of it. (well at least it should pay me 2 month wages I will have invested in the end)http://www.forexfactory.com/images/icons/icon12.gif

Thats a good point MJ - Most threads will give an illusion as to the real success rate of a system....

The people who had/have succesful trades will be quick to post a chart and picture "bragging" (in a way) about their trade - when the 10 people who lost trades "bragging" about it will be the last thing on their minds and so they won't post the trade they lost on...

In the end we are left with a whole lotta winners and very few losers being posted creating this sort of illusion. It happens in all threads and is a very good point to make.

I think this is a big trap of most threads

1 Bot Feches rates for all

1 Bot fetches Interest Rates for all

Spud and MJ,

Here is Spud's system that I'am currently testing and it seems to be working

pretty good, but I'am still tweeking.

Manual trading:

1).  5m chart. (only 1 chart and time frame).

2).  Spuds stoch rope system (6-1-1---24-1-1).

3).  a crossover sma system on the price.

a).  2 sma, hloc/4.

b).  4 or 5 sma, hloc/4.

c).  30sma hloc/4 for the trend, don't trade against.

What I have found is, when the stoch's start to break down / up and

we get a crossover of the 2sma across the 5sma the move seem to

go in our direction...I'am using the turn of the stoch's as my exit.

It's more of a scalping system but it is very accurate.

--- 帖子 #1419 ---
Attatched is screen shot and my interpretation of a multi stoch indi to match Spud's rules of closed bar values. It has user controls for 5 different stochs, can be different time frames and or different stoch settings. Defaults are:

all use simple and Low/High but user can also change those

stoch M5 14,1,1 yellow

stoch M15 14,3,3 white

stoch M30 14,3,3 aqua

stoch H1 14,3,3 royal blue

stoch H4 14,3,3, red

These will appear as stair steps, each stoch line carries the same value until the newest bar is closed in that stoch's time frame. The exception to that is if the chart time frame matches the stoch time frame then that line will wag with real time price changes. Note that lines for stoch time frames smaller than the chart time frame will not appear, that is you will not see a stoch M5 on charts longer than M5.  This is easy to load since one indicator file makes all 5 lines at one time.

Feedback is welcome.

Attached File(s)   DME_HM_5Stoch1Line.mq4

6 KB
|
744 downloads

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #1422 ---
Sorry it doesn't just jump out at you!

I wish you were a bit more descript about what you don't get.

Spud's rules are to look at stoch values from the last closed price bar of the chart time frame the stoch is for.  That is why he has individual time charts for each of the stochs he wants to follow.

I have seen two different indicators to show multiple TF stochs on one indicator window.  Both had some draw backs for how I want to use them.  For instance the indi "All Stochastics"  will paint the stoch lines bar showing the curves as they would with stochs on their individual price charts however the data points do not line up with the price bars above them except for the most recent.  If I want to study past possible trades I can't because the stoch position in history does not align with price.

The other nifty indicator is "#MTF Multi Stochastic".  This one will have the current stoch points wag with real time price move making it difficult to judge where the closing stoch values were, have to drag cursor carefully to correct price for each different stoch to see the value so very time consuming if wanting to study historical trades.  Because the current plot wagging it is less than ideal to judge current entries also.  This one also interpolates where stoch might have been between price points so we have a smoothed line between the closed bars.  I assume it is obvious, the stoch plot of close prices for M15 stoch when plotted on M5 price chart has only one stoch value for every 3 price bars.

My version will show the closed stoch value, the value Spud uses for entry determinations, until a new closed value arrives based on the time frame of each stoch.  So on a M5 chart there will be one M5 stoch data piont for each price bar, 3 M15 stoch data points for each M5 price bar, 6 M30 stoch data points for each M5 price bar, 12 H1 stoch data points for each M5 price bar and 48 H4 stoch data points for each M5 price bar.

The current plot of all higher time frame stochs will not wag, it will show the last closed stoch plot.  The exception is the stoch time frame matching the current price chart will wag with real time data movement.

I hope that helps. If not then put my indi on a M5 chart next to price charts for M15, H1, H4 with their stochs and compare a few data points between my indi and those higher time frame charts.

--- 帖子 #1433 ---
chehab,

The white line of your single stoch plot on chart time M15 has an opening bar time of 23:15 (Eastern+7, same as my broker).  I believe the current M5 bar on your chart has start time 23:25.  That would be in the middle time range of the M15 chart bar that started at 23:15.

That bar will stay open for 15 minutes and in that time that stochastic can wag up and down with price.

My indicator will only plot values of the higher time frame stochastics based on closed bars for each of their time frames.  So in this case any time from 23:15 up til the end of 23:29 the white line of my indicator will show you the stoch value from the M15 chart for bar labeled with start time 23:00 because that bar is the last closed bar on the M15 chart.  It closed a second before 23:15.   This would also be true for the M30 stoch, H1 stoch and H4 stoch but each has it's own bar close time, sometimes they line up to be the same time.  For instance every time the H4 bar closes all the charts below that time frame will also close.  But every time a lower time frame bar closes it does not necessarily mean the higher time frames bars are also closing.

Make your M15 chart candles as wide as possible and place the cursor on the M15 stoch line exactly at the 23:00 bar and read the stoch value in a little data box that appears or open the View>Data Window and view the value there when your sursor is on the 23:00 bar.

--- 帖子 #1437 ---
just some thoughts.

playing around with different filters it basically boils down to this:

As I mentioned in some posts much earlier my feeling about too much filtering seems to get more and more confirmed.

I know we all strive to get close to 100% success rate.

But in fact that might not be the most profitable thing to do.

1. imaging we could filter all bad trades so that only good once are entered

POSITIVE would be: we could place all our money on such a trade

NEGATIVE: there would be properly not many trades and our TP would be just a few PIPs (but ith a great value)

(I doubt that we can do that 100% and get still a meaningful number of trades).

2. as we properly do not get a guaranteed 100% success rate we might go for a very close to 100% (say 95-98%) one.

Actually I think this is with filtering possible: but the problem is that we might filter out so many trades that we are still left with just a couple and as we are having not a 100% success rate - one loser might wipe out much of our profit.

3. we might not filter out so many trades - which leaves us with much more looser but also more winners (hopefully).

I have seen all of such 3 option (well just for a short time for 100% ;-)

The real art is to find the best overall ration.

If one does not filter - even if the overall ration might be successful - the problem will remain that we get many winners but also many looser - which makes it difficult to commit a good amount of money per trade as one must expect a couple of looser in a row.

Trying too much filtering is still enticing (graving for risk free trading): The problem is: is there ever a chance of being 100% sure (which to my understanding is not)

So the real aim - I would suggest is to follow what produces the most profit over a good amount of time. (taking into account a reasonable risk)

MJ

--- 帖子 #1438 ---
cubicrey,

I see two problems.

1) The M5 stoch on your template is set to 14,3,3 whereas Spud's rules and my stoch show 14,1,1 just for the M5 stoch.

2) The big problem however is the method of offsetting the higher time frame plots on the faster chart, in this case the M5 chart.

If you would read my two postings explaining my method and then compare your stoch displays to separate higher time frame charts you would also see the problem.

Each candle or price bar represents a period of time for instance a candle on M15 chart lasts for 15 minutes of time and the label associated with that price bar is the starting time for that bar, not the ending time.  The close price of a CLOSED candle is the price at the end of the time period associated with that candles label.  For instance am M15 bar labeled 21:15 has data starting at 21:15 and ending at 21:29:60.   One second more and a new price bar starts.

Historical indicator plots are showing values based on closed bars.

On an M15 chart a normal, regular, non time shifted stochastic will show a stoch value based on data through the CLOSE of M15 21:29:00 not the start of 21:15.

The stochastic value of M15 bar labeled 21:15 is not available until 21:29:00.

My plots will show the value seen on chart M15 at label 21:15 and plot it on M5 chart starting at 21:30 for 3 bars since 21:30 is when the M15 chart started a new bar, the prior bar was closed and the complete data was available.

Your version is plotting the value from a closed higher time frame bar at a time in that bar's past on the lower time frame chart which is invalid and can lead to false conclusions if backtesting with those lines.

For instance EURUSD Jan 13, 2009 10:30 GMT+2 (my broker chart time) M15 chart at Spud's settings is 52.3962.

On my chart you see that same value plotted on M5 chart at times 10:45, 10:50, 10:55.  On an M5 chart the close of bar labeoled 10:55 will also signify the start of the next M15 bar.

On your chart this same stoch value 52.3962 is plotted at M5 chart times 10:30, 10:35, 10:40.  This is wrong because that value did not exist until 10:45.

I hope this does the trick for you.

--- 帖子 #1439 ---
This is the key.

Thanks for your time and clarification.

Reyna.

--- 帖子 #1441 ---
If you put your cursor line on each bar and then look at the stoch value it is correct for each bar.  The sloped line is connecting those valid price points.  The plot is accurate.  In order to put a vertical line in place would mean that whenever there is a stoch value change there would have to be two stoch values ploted on one time bar which does not really make sense.  For instance to have a vertical line from say stoch 45% to 48% you would have to have both of those values on the same bar.

This indicator is using the time series plotting ability of MT4.  It is the way all time series is ploted using an array, one value per time bar.  To do what you ask would require an entirely different method to paint the info, manually using objects and I believe very messy, lots of work and for value I don't see.

--- 帖子 #1470 ---
englesh,inglish... dem...aha:

jump ship

to leave a job or activity suddenly. Although most of our employees are satisfied with their jobs, half of them would probably jump ship if something becames available elsewhere. The original star of the TV series jumped ship after the first season.

Usage notes: often said about someone who goes to work for another company

(idiom) To depart a project without warning.

Etymology: based on the literal meaning of jump ship (= to leave a ship without permission while it is temporarily in a port in the middle of a trip)

See also: jump, ship
Cambridge Dictionary of American Idioms  Cambridge University Press 2003

--- 帖子 #1477 ---
Hi, I Have been using the "#MTF Multi Stochastic" indicator for over a year now ans what I do is go to properties /colours and change the settings so that 1 and 2 are the same colour and on colour 2, set the style to dotted.

What this does is show the wagging portion of the stoch line as a dotted line so its easy to see which part of the relevant stochastic has closed and which hasn't.

On a  different note, I think that regardless of what strategy you follow that works for you, there is probably room for MTF stochastics. I can say that when i trade against MTF stochastics (inadvertantly), the trade will fail or stall or both almost universally.

I think Spud has proven to be one of the more genuine and usefull contributors on FF and guess what? He is one of the few if not the only one that hasn't tried to make money out of his work innovations. For that I thank him!

Using Spud's MTF Stos method keeps you away from large drawdowns (or even losses if you can't sustain the pressure). Using the M5 and M1 together to define the entry, in relation to the M15/M30 move will give you a very good entry point. The DD will on depend on how many pips you want to cash in and how far you want to go in the risk --> if you escalate your profits using the longer TF (H1, H4), you will anyway increase your risk (DD). Hi Spud,

First time poster, long time reader of all your threads.  Really appreciate all the time you've spent educating.

I'm an emini trader and have adapted your ideas, just using different time frames (5/15/45/135/D).  30/60 don't divide well into the emini 8:30 CST to 13:15 session, thus 45/135.

Your talk about M# has to rise for H# to continue going down made me wonder if there is a way to determine odds if M# is going to continue rising, causing H# to come up (reversal)?  Or will M# reverse and H# will continue going down (continuation).

It is easy to compute the closing price it would take to change the stochastic direction of any given time frame (M15, M30, H1, H4, D)?

Given current price, the price required to change stochastic direction, the size of the average price movement per time frame, and how much time is remaining in the current bar per time frame, it would seam odds of a pullback/continuation or reversal could be made.

Curious what you think and if you have done any experiments in that area?

--- 帖子 #1493 ---

--- 帖子 #1503 ---
Thanks.

there are a couple of thoughts I want to share related to what you said.

1. persevering: YES I believe too many traders switch too fast their ideas.

On the other hand Spud's MTF stochs had some special things I liked:

a. Spud presented it in a very good way.

b. Putting all related ideas together: there were enough parameters around to play with - and still having a basic common idea.

c. It was not a fixed rule set ' but an idea to play with' as one can see in the many different presentations of Spud himself.

d. early test showed that maybe it could really work out

---------------

This are some of the 'things' I found attractive and which took me captivated to persevere.

---------------

e. Because of that I did very intensive programming: and you know -- if one invests more time (or other resources) into something - it is also more likely that one will not so easily give up.

f. it is also the first trading bot which is solemnly based on price action and TA

g. and because of the complexity it has become the most advanced (in a technical programming way not necessarily in return) trading bot I did so far

---------------

So, kind of developed a special 'love' for this piece of program: which also helped to persevere.

---------------

2. RISK/REWARD RATION: Depending?

Win/Loss ration is ok - but that can also deceive in some cases: One might get a 99% Win and 1 % Loss ration but still be a looser depending on the used Unit Size and TP and SL settings.

e.g 99 x 1 Unit 1 PIP TP  -  1 x 200 Units 200 SL

RISK/REWARD:  In my opinion it is simply like that: an account MUST be able to make in a reasonable time a new HIGH (I would hope at least once a month - but if the strategy has less trades maybe at least once in 2 month).

So, if a draw-down is so much that by the giving strategy (in average) I can not achieve such New High  - it is doomed to fail. I'm not going to wait 3 years until I get a new High.

So, MoneyManagment is also an important part to fit a strategy.

For instance for Spud's MTF stochs I used first only a simple MM - later I applied some of my usual fixed programed and good MM.

But in the end I did change that: as for this strategy it seemed to be a bit contra-productive.

Why: because there are still some: JUST WRONG signals - which I can not filter away. And sometimes these would get very high Units Size  assigned to.

In the light of a relatively good Win/Loss %: In using a more simple different MM I could improve the return.

I think this is important:
RISK/REWARD:  an account MUST be able to make in a REASONABLE time a new HIGH: And you are right.

probably I could increase the trading size and squeezes out quite a bit more: on my live account I aim at the moment for 30 % per year with Spud's MTF. (but I can imaging it up to 200 % per year if it runs well and some MM adjustments accordingly).

But for the first year one does not have to push it to the limit: so 20% with reasonable DrawDown till end of December is OK for me

Hi all,

I have been reading Spud's thread with avid interest and I have a question that I hope someone can answer.

Apologies in advance for asking a question about an old post in this thread but this post really has me puzzled.

The post is "The Balls"...

http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...&postcount=206

In particular, this part of the post in which Spud says...

"So why do I expect the red ball to fall. Because M15 and M30 (blue and purple balls) can't build H1 downwards where they are. The M15 and M30 balls have to go up first. They may only go up 20%..they may go up 80%..we don't know. What we do know is that for M15 and M30 to rise, M5 has to fall down to get a long trigger (best) or at least go down far enough to raise M15 and M30."

What I don't get is that "for M15 and M30 to rise M5 has to fall down to get a long trigger (best) or at least go down far enough to raise M15 and M30.

If say the red ball bounced around for say a dozen bars above say the 70% level then wouldn't you also expect to see M15 and M30 rise?

I am having trouble getting my head around the statement that for M15 and M30 to rise then M5 must fall. Intuitively I would expect that for M15 and M30 to rise then M5 must rise also?

I have a feeling that I am missing something very simple here but I cannot for the life of me figure out what it is.

Thanks in advance.

Laurence.

Hi lhookway,

just first: I'm no expert in stochs - and I did not focus at all on the Ball presentation (kinda skipped it .

But I can share how I think:

I think that is the clue.

How can M5 rise (when it is on the top ?)

it first must go down (at least a little bit), doesn't it.

But it can be observed that smaller time frames make much more often total circles than higher time frames stochs. So, it can be expected that the smaller time frame might make a number of up, down circles before the higher make one.

Well, as I say no expert on Ball's  - but maybe it helps to get a other persons thoughts.

My thoughts are like that:

I think that this may give the wrong impression: that escalator does not give bad signals.

So, I think one would have to say: Stochastic (like any other indicator) may give at times wrong signals: My experience is: There are at time JUST PLAIN WRONG. I could filter much out in one of systems which I use live: But from time to time there are still some of this total wrong signals.

Until now I could not find any useful ways to get rid of such remaining: and make the trading still worthwhile.

I think it depends a lot of how one uses the stochs.

Also if the trading is manual or automatized.

In my case: I do not use any other indicators for now: Only stochs and price-actions: I use TP and SL on each trade and never change them after a trade is executed.

I may change this in my new testing based more on a EscalatorToPips version. But I think, if I would change my fixed SL I would opt for a dynamic trailing SL .

Anyway for this new testing it is much to early to say anything - most of it is still negative.

--- 帖子 #1520 ---
Hello,

I personaly tested a lot of EA's. Some delivering interesting results (but only working either in trends or ranging markets), some completely choppy just as the market can be, some loosing a lot. I would advise you to make a working EA on lower TF than D1 just because the EA will not trade much and without much trades you don't have enough trades to be sure your EA is working. And, according to me, once you've got a good strategy, it should work on the main TF, from M15 to D1.

ABout SL, I would use a limited SL (20 to 35 pips, if it's more it's because the entry is not accurate enough), trailing should be higher to give some room to the trade and be sure to make money even if your strategy is a 50% winner, ... the best is to use a dynamic stop (MA, ADX, ...).

To be completely honest, I believe in EA's to facilitate your life but not to be 100% automatic as I said above, your EA will not perform the same in all the market conditions and the human intelligence is difficult to put in an EA, but that's only my personal view!

Hope it helps!

Continue trying, it's the only way to beat the forex dealer!

--- 帖子 #1521 ---
I forgot to mention that yu should add a BE in your EA, not to far from your entry point. TO be finetuned according to your strategy.

KDR

--- 帖子 #1522 ---
Hi PipPicker, sorry I did not see your message.

I would suggest to open a trade only when the ADX signal is climbing and above let's say 25. ADX+ should of course be above ADX-. And the MTF STOS should be climbing for a buy/declining for a sell. The ADX signal will allow you to trade only when the trend is effective (the trend is your friend). If ADX is below 25, no trade or range trading only (using RSI or STOS or Bollinger...).

I also like to have the moving averages properly aligned and not in spaghetti. You can also use the MTF STOS patterns to better feel what's happening and confirm with ADX.

I'm still in the process of analysing ADX in combination with MTF STOS. I'm convinced in can clearly help in your trade decisions. I'm using it for 3 weeks now on my real account and I perform much better than without using it.

Good luck!

I really like multiple time frame analysis as it is simple and straight forward. I pretty much know this system only and find it pretty tough to learn others as i have heard of great results from people using it.

The main problem with stochastics and MTF i feel is that there are a high precentage of winners. I have maintained at least a 80% ever since i started with it. The main problem is when my losers kick in. They are usually large, very large. I don't know how to reduce this. People have gave me solutions to it which was to have a predefined stop lost but then by having one I usually find myself with more loosing trades as the market fluctuates more than anticipated.

Anther problem in dealing with MTF is the signals that each timeframe gives. When I trade the MTF i use 3 screens. The first screen I go with a MACD and stochas and some emas and BB. I figure out the trend here on the highest time frame. After that i go to second time frame which is 5 minute and then I look for stochastics to be point in the same direction as the first time frame. but the thing is after i spot a trend, on first TF, it usually gives me little time to enter as the 5 min stochs quicly goes OVERBOUGHT. The stochastics are giving me a great headache with the quick overbought or oversold position everything there is a quick move. I am not really sure how others are dealing with this cuz at certain time prices continue to go further in the direction of oversold and overbought and when this happens, i don't know when the price action will reverse and change. Anyone can help me out to figure when to determine in and out?

MTF Stochastic:

My main Time frames are M1, M5 (I use both as Entries (and trade management) but M1 has more weight for me than the M5)  and in addition M15 and H1.

I also look at times at the H4 and daily charts.

I use some variations of The  Rope, and I'm aware of Escalator to Pips setups (but very seldom have the guts to let the profit run) and have in-cooperated some MACD stuff and some Moving Average.

I also give a little bit attention to general price candles formation (chart pattern) and general areas of resistance.

All together I trade short term mostly a couple of pips at the time.

One of my current weaknesses are:

I take profit mostly to quick instead of letting it run a bit longer and also let loosing trades run far too long.

I guess this is partially one of the side effects of not trading by strict rules.

Maybe first I have to say that the posting you quoted was from a time where I did a fully automated trading.

I had a system which checked so many parameters: even Spud's 'Rope'

it worked quite ok but had mainly this problems: very few trades per week even though I checked many pairs.

And on the other side there where from time and time entries which more or less immediately turned wrong and hit SL.

But as I said - all together it was quite ok - the main reason why I stopped it: was that I had planned to move to an other broker and also an other important reason was that there where very few trades per week by quite small TP (15-30pips)

In the mean time I did not change my broker and so I thought to do a bit more manual trading instead of programming. Manually I have to take a different approach as it is impossible to keep track of all my automated parameter.

Spending more screen time gives me also a new feeling for it and might be of an advantage in case I do again some automated trading programming.

The one thing from Spud's teaching which is very strongly impressed on my mind is:  LOWER time frames BUILD HIGHER.

Anyway, I would not be extreme on either position as even in Spud's teaching some aspect go to the (Longer time frames lead the shorter)

--- 帖子 #1564 ---
hi despichtt,

Well the indicator I had in mind had also some problems.

Anyway: I did some changes for you.

I think I did a fast hack of what you wanted.

BUT there is some general problems involved with this -  it is important that you are aware of it.

Let's assume you plot on a 15 min chart. The 15 min StochBar should be correct and update with the live candle.

If you plot a higher TimeFrame StochBar you get such problem.

e.g. 30 min Stoch.

On a 15 min chart you get 2 bars for  ONE 30min bar.

Here is the problem: when the first bar of the 2 finishes - it has one  particular color - let's assume 'DownTrend' (in the new version the  correct color at that time as it changes color with the live active candle)

But what happens if in the next 15min the 30min stoch actually  turns up and at the end of the 30min candle  it has a ' UpTrend'

So you get your second bar on the 15min chart as 'UpTrend'.

Now you have the problem that your PAST candle is not any more correct in the light of the finished 30min candle.

There should be 2 "UpTrend bars" on the 1 min Chart.

But you got: 1 "DownTrend bar' and 1 "UpTrend bar"

Just that you are aware of it.

The actual bars are correct (except I made a mistake   ) at the time when the chart's candle (in our e.g. 15min) closed.

I hope you got my point.

I also added an additional color in the rare case that a stoch is  neither up nor down but flat  (only in between overbought and oversold area)

I did not checkmuch  if all works correct  - as this takes time until the higher time-frames stochs update.

Just try the attached indicator - if it does what you where looking for.

/*

HLines and Trendlines are supported

To activate them: you need first to draw them on the chart and then use there names ( to assign here )

if empty it is not included

--- 帖子 #1576 ---
The whole story; here it is..

About Stochastics:

I did a lot of short term trading in the past basicly on a 1min frame. My basic indicator has always been Stochastics. Its important to know all figures and understand what happened for the figure to became what it is. Since I’ve seen all figures on a rapid base watching 1min charts so often, I’m very familiar to all setups. I now use all knowledge on all timeframes. I use additional signals, besides from switching color bars, from stochastics for entrée and also for exit.

For special figures especially from 5 and 15min frame I use the confirming color from the TF’s as an entrée as well(don’t care for the color of 30min and H4 in this case). So if you see both lines deverging down from price and have confirming red bars after a 5min candle has closed. Its important to know if market is trending or not to know how to read the behaviour of stochastics. If you see market is trending up you switch thinking and start reading information from the bottoms in stead of from the peaks. This can give you valuable information on how strong the trend and if its likely to continue or not.

I wont bother you too much with all ins and outs(I can tolk for hours on the story) but I think one should know all from its main instrument.

MTF Stochastics:

If I talk about the balk it’s the area between 0-20 and 80-100; balk line: 20 and 80(from snooker!). I use 5min as main setup. MTF stochastics 5, 15, 30min and H4 in color bars and MTF Stochastics v2.0 for visualisation. I use some EMA’s for messuring strength of trend and to adjust stops. Most of the time I place my stops in between the 12 and 24 EMA. Emloyed Pivots Points and Trend Hull, that’s all.

Basicly: Look for situations where all color is green or red on the Stochastics color bar setup. Situation has to hold until the Candle from 5min closes. Reload Template from time to time. Important: CandleStick patterns(engulfing, doji’s, breakout patterns etc).

15/30 min cannot be overbought for going long/not oversold for going short(unless 5minStoch moved fast to the other side on little price change, typical in a trend with more to come). 4H have to be out of Balk if want to go long/short. H4 overbought is fine for going long as is H4 oversold for going short(all other lines no extreme values).

Pre-Announcements by the Bigger TF’s are often strong signals(15/30min announcing pre on the 5min: divergence!). Strong: 5/15/30 “Bundel” forces towards target. Little price chance and more inline colors from Stochastics is good building. All 5, 15 als 30Min Stochastics on groen/rood makes a strong case as well. If 4H crosses from balk to balk you see very nice crossings from 5 and 15minStoch; 15min leaving balk inline the crossing H4 is also a very str case. 5min overb/s not a problem if there is much room for the 15 and 30min to go and some very nice bias. If both 5 and 15min deverging > act on the confirming color if it’s a definite candle(cannot switch back from color). 5 and 30 getting green at the same time while 15 already green but H4 still in Balk balk is good to trade.

I always try to make smal improvements on price. Exit on a contra color bar from 15(Focus Stoch)/30min; exit on signal line theory from Spud or divergence from 5min Stochastics. In overb/s situations: tighten Stop. If 15 or 30min start to twinkle from color: shorten your stop as well. Adjust Stop and profit target to the scale of the currunt volatility(look at the changing scale of the chart).

I always evaluate the setup from all lines from Stochastics. It’s a bit of a grafity story in most cases. I than decide if it’s a weak or strong setup. Weak to me are situations where the action is below the H4 Stochastics and a short setup takes place. I like 15 and 30 both reaching the Balk area from 50 level at the same time(pipping time!). I take profit or shorten stop much faster on weak setups. Strong play’s: aim for Pivots or other sup/res/trend lines. Situations where H4 is crossing from balk to balk are often strong as well.

How wrong I would have been.. I have to say it was a weak setup at this time but I could have taken this trade. --- 帖子 #1615 ---
Here it goes: UniversalStochastic_MainK_mj_v1.14.mq4

This is universal multifunctional stochastic.

As related to Spuds teaching: Only the K% Main Stochastic is calculated: (No D% line).

I hope it works as hoped for.

This will be my replacement for all stochastics I have used so far: No other one is any-more needed. (that's why: Universal)

Short Note of the options:

ShowBars=true : Displays color bars - if false it displays the Stoch Line

ConsiderColorOverBoughtSold=true;  Related to Bars Display: uses for Oversold/Overbought additional Color ( In that area there is no direction check)

If false: Direction Check is everywhere and only UP, DOWN, FLAT color are used.

UseInterpolation: Uses for stochastic interpolation - can also be used with Color Bars (probably quite useful)

Related to the next option: if Interpolation is enabled we readjust always Data correctly (Hopefully

ReAdjustDataForPastBars=true;  (if true Past Data are ReAdjusted (Line and Bars)

if false and no Interpolation is used: there should be no readjustment of Data (you see this only after some time with new data coming in (at first initialization all past data are correctly (hopefully)

set to false can be also a useful option

DontDisplayValuesAndSettings=false; if true: Values in the indicator window are not displayed: quite useful for instances where one uses multiple stochastics overlayed:

like the Rope or so MTF 4 or 5 stochastics.

Take a look at the pic for some more info

--- 帖子 #1619 ---
hi,

I did some more work on the Universal Stochastic. Highlighted the most important changes.

UStochastic_mj_v1.08.mq4

Other changes:

1. Shorten name to UStochastic (Universal Stochastic)

2. Less Warning alerts - some sensible adjustments internally.

3. Display more setting info

4. simplified code
5. Added four possible Alerts. Just a NOTE: you can use the alerters also with Bar display.
6. Added again D% Line to make it more universal (but it must be actively enabled)

7. Added option to disable DisableLowerStochPeriodAlert Warning: But still drop the display on purpose
8. Attached again an easy past copy template for MTF and Rope:

New_Example_MTF_and__Rope__mj.tpl

I don't know how resource intense my stoch version is compared to the plain one: if you have many charts with 30-50 stochs  who knows.

(so I would enable the DLine only if I really want to use it.)

___________________
ALERT INFO:

What does it mean:

CrossesAbove: Stoch was before AT or BELOW set value and is now above it.

CrossesBelow: Stoch was before AT or ABOVE set value and is now below it.

NOTE: one can also use decimal points as Spud did: e.g. 23.6,76.4

Alerter does only consider the Main K% Line

e.g. scenario:

1.
One wants to be alerted whenever the Stoch crosses above or below the 50 level

note19="==ALERTS CROSSES ABOVE==";

Alert1_CrossesAbove=50;

Alert2_CrossesAbove=0;

note20="==ALERTS CROSSES BELOW==";

Alert1_CrossesBelow=50;

Alert2_CrossesBelow=0;

2.
One wants to be alerted whenever the Stoch crosses above overbought level 80, crosses below overbought level 80

crosses below oversold level 20, crosses above oversold level 20

NOTE: That case was why I decided on 4 possible alerts.

note19="==ALERTS CROSSES ABOVE==";

Alert1_CrossesAbove=80;

Alert2_CrossesAbove=20;

note20="==ALERTS CROSSES BELOW==";

Alert1_CrossesBelow=80;

Alert2_CrossesBelow=20;

NOTE:  in the case above you can get a number of alerts if the stoch wiggle up and down the 80 (as you have set  CrossesAbove=80 and CrossesBelow=80)

TIP: if you play around with same StochPeriod/Slowing but different things like interpolation you can add something to: UniquePrefix to distinquish them in the Alert popup message.

___________

Picture shows the K% AND new D% line extended til active chart bar.

--- 帖子 #1622 ---
hi jacksonphili,

Spud tried to show some  ways/ideas to extend profit and I guess he probably did it quite well.

I'm not so sure if Spud was really teaching milking the market to  the maximum: he often refereed to 20 pips a day goal and his Pip bank  (if I remember correctly: it's  a long time I really read through the  thread)

But as in many threads the emphasis is more on the good setups (I also think that is correct - no point to show and teach only by failed examples .

But this gives often a kind of slightly distorted view: I can not speak for Spud, but I know from others (some have posted here) that after some time they move on because the success-rate was not what they expected.

Many people trade systems only from one chart so in general I would say 3 charts can work out quite well. But I would guess it depends what one really does on/with this 3 charts (or 1 chart).

BTW: making 8-10 pips is also not easy: as the final success will depend on many other factors: like success rate, how big is the SL loss if it really hits (e.g One  50 pis SL eats away 5 10 pips successes - also we pay spread cost which is in relation to smaller pips a higher percentage, Money Management etc. etc)

To give a closer answer to your question: I would say demo trade for a couple of month with 3 charts after that you will be able to give yourself some answer which will be more worthy than if 10 people tell you it will work. (or it won't work.

I wish you all the best on your trading journey

--- 帖子 #1642 ---
Primary indies used :

MTF_Stoch : Black lines placed in M5 chart with M15 stoch.

CCI : White line placed in the same indicator window, with +200 & -200 levels in white.

MACD : Red line in the same window. The MACD plays a vital role in entry. Using MACD with Stochs was the original idea of Nanningbobs.

BIG Picture : Thanks to Favorite for this big picture idea to decide whether to go long or short. You must read his thred at

http://www.forexfactory.com/showthre...14566&page=169

Favorite M1 chart method of scalping is also good and he has been doing it successfully. You can understand the importance of deciding the trend at any point of time during the day trading.

ENTRY : All the above three indicators come together above the +200 or below the -200 level of CCI. Around this area there is first signal given be the mtf_stoch.

After the arrow appears just wait for the next two M5 candles complete. Opening of the 4th candle entry can be made.

EXIT : The MACD & the mtf_stoch will travel across to the other end straight or with some oscillation. Just hang on until these two reach the other side and there you exit the trade. You can also exit when the market crosses the Trend Magic indi.

If you patience, You can follow through the trade until the market crosses the HAS 2 9 2 12.

There were too many other indicators I gave earlier. Now I think all of them will confuse more. So I have minimized to what is just required for entry & exit in order to maintain the chart clean as also be KISS.

Fx....$

The only indicator I use to trade is stochastics. I don't see a need to use anything else, except maybe volume.

I've learned to trade stochastics successfully on any time frame as low as 1 minute, and through my trials and errors, I've learned (the hard way) that there is no magical indicator that can tell you what to do. The sooner you accept this, the sooner you can start to improve your trading. There are indicators that happen to work better than others (in certain situations), but the real "magic" lies in knowing how to use the indicators the "right" way, and also when.

And I am pretty sure the "right" way couldn't be more clear than in the title of this thread...

short audusd @ .9283 6:15 pst took screen shot at entry time- so far right candle

=

How read my Stoch setup--

Red line = 5min

Yellow line = 15 min

Small broken lines ---------------- = 30 min

Med broken lines --- - --- - --- = 1 hour

Long broken lines__ __ __ __ __ =4 hour

Set up for long is wait for the red line to cross 10 %

Enter trade when 15min yellow line turns up along with price

*price must be higher then when the red line first crossed 10%.----Messed up here on this trade :-0

**Reverse for shorts

##Exit when the 15min yellow line turns against the trade and bar closes.

--- 帖子 #1672 ---
“Stochastics is a momentum oscillator,” said Lane. -The Father of stochastics- “It doesn’t follow price, it doesn’t follow volume or anything like that. It follows the speed or the momentum of price. As a rule, the momentum changes direction before price.”
He made a comparison to a rocket speeding away from the Earth. Before the rocket can turn and head back to the ground again, it must first start to slow down.

here is the full interview

--- 帖子 #1674 ---
Hello Pip,

Purely for the sake of clarity, when 5 (and 3 on some pairs) places of decimals were introduced into FX pricing the final number became a point, which equates to 1/10th or 0.1 of a pip.  Some platforms actually show the points in red or a smaller font size to lessen the confusion.  Your example above, therefore, equates to 92668 minus 92546 which = 122 points or 12.2 pips.

I hope that helps.

TTFN

Merlyn
